O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	 O you, very dear son, I have completed this book which is the end of the science of medicine together with its practice, and I have made the end through its explanations and by its statements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	 And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of the hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	 And because the work of the hands is rejected in our region and is foreign to all, the science has perished and decayed, and nothing remains of it except for small descriptions in the books of the ancients that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	 And from this come errors and vanities, and intentions are closed off and science is distanced.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	 And it seems to me that I wish to bring this treatise to life according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will also include the forms of cautery tools, and other instruments of the work with their explanation and preparation as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	 And for this reason, because no good hand surgeons are found in our time, the art of medicine is neglected.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	 And it is necessary that he who undertakes this should excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, to know the judgment of the members and their forms and connections and separations, and have knowledge of the bones and nerves and muscles and the number of them, and their movement and rest, and the place from which they originate.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	 And for this reason says Hippocrates that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little; and likewise in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	 We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable in the things mentioned before, should take care not to fall into error and harm people; as I have seen many times those who engage in this science and then abandon their learning and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	 For I saw a foolish doctor who cut into an abscess of scrofula on the neck of a woman, and cut into the arteries of the neck; therefore so much blood came out that the woman fell dead in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	 And I saw another doctor who removed a stone from a man with water, and the stone was large; so he took away with it a piece of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	 And I had already been called for it to be extracted, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if one removed it he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	 And I saw another doctor who took care of the Duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break there was a wound; and the doctor, full of ignorance, pulled the fracture onto the wound to the splints with great force, and did not leave any bandage on the wound, and left it like this for a term; and he commanded that it should not be released; and so it remained until the leg was completely swollen and the foot came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	 I was called to go to him, and I hastened to go and release the leg; and when I had released it, he was in peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	 But still the corruption was already confirmed in the limb, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to spread throughout the limb until the limb was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	 And another physician saw that an abscess had been opened and then inflamed due to the evil nature of its ruler.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	 For chancre, when it is purified of black bile, one must not touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that one can completely remove what is corrupt.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	 And therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: namely, works where there is danger in many situations; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	 Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	 Galiens said in some of his admonitions: “Do not take on incurable diseases, lest you be called a foolish physician.”
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	 The first chapter is about fire cautery and about cautery with medicinal water, and this chapter is arranged from the head down to the feet; about the forms of instruments, and the tools for cautery, and everything that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	 The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about cupping and wounds, and about the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is arranged about the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	 The third chapter concerns the restoration of dislocations and sprains, and similar things; it is organized from the head down to the feet, and concerning the shapes of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	 As we recall the work, it is necessary for me to explain the quality of the aid and the harm of each temperament.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	 I say that the quality of aid and harm is the longest speech and most subtle science and secret response; and many wise men have spoken about this and agreed on it; but their words suffice me little, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	 I say that cautery universally helps all temperaments where there is material, except for two temperaments: namely, hot temperament without material, and dry temperament without material.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	 En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, some people have debated and said that cautery is of great help here; and others have said the opposite: that cautery is not effective against diseases caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	 Because the nature of fire is hot and should not be treated with heat or dryness; and he who speaks against this says that cautery is of great help for hot and dry diseases in the human body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	 Because when you compare the body of man and his moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	 And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	 Because I have found it to be true through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	 And indeed, let none interfere except for those who have experienced it, and who know by long practice the chapter on cauteries, and the diversity of men's complexions, and their dispositions and causes of diseases, and the occurrences and time span; we do not fear other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	 And all the doctors agreed on the use of cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	 And know, son, that a fire cautery is among the secrets of cures, and of greater benefit than a hot medicine cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	 For fire is simple, and does not affect any other member except the one being treated, if it can be avoided.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	 The burning medicines spread from one member to another, causing serious illness in the affected member; and by chance, they can kill the patient. The fire, due to its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not do this unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	 I have found this through experiment and the length of my service and study in the art, based on the truth of things; and for that reason, I excuse myself for the length of the speech, because it does not please me that I take away the secret which is revealed in fire, and the quality of the work, how it expels diseases from the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; now receive this in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	 And know, son, that they agreed on what time they should be made, the cauteries, and chose patients.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	 And I say that a cautery is necessary in all times, because the harm that comes is put to rest by the aid of the cautery; and especially if the cautery is for pains which are urgent and pressing so that they cannot wait until greater evil comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	 And do not ever think so, dear son, as the foolish doctors do; for the illness which is healed by a cautery has no relapse; and they say it thus; but it is not so as they believe, because a cautery is nothing other than medicine that changes the complexion, and dries the humors that are the cause of the pain, and it is more useful than medicine for its swift effectiveness, and for the virtue of its work and power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	 And it can happen that the disease comes sometimes according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the illness and its strength; and superfluous things are gathered in him through the acquisition of food and similar things, unless cauteries are administered in the place where there is little superfluity and moisture, such as tooth cauteries for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	 And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last resort of medicine, and it is true; but they do not believe that cautery is worth after medicine, but their thoughts are false, and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we administer ways of cures in any illness and they do not work, then we administer the cautery, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	 Then it is clear that cauterization is the last resort in medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	 The ancients said that cauterization with gold is better than with iron, and they said this not only because of the quality of gold but also because of its high value; and they said that the place of cautery does not become infected, but this is not true, for I have experienced it and found that it is true in some men; and cauterization with gold is better than with iron, as they used to say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	 And yet when you heat the gold instrument, you do not know when it is hot enough by the color of the gold, and it cools quickly; and if one heats it too much, it burns in the fire; and thus there are many hindrances.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	 Et pour cela, nous utilisons le cautère du feu, qui est bien adapté à notre travail.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	 And for this reason, I have arranged this chapter from the head to the feet, so that it may be easier to find what you are looking for.
dou cautere olivaire	 about olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	 This cautery is used for moisture and cold on the head, and there are two kinds that are done because of an illness called "soda," and because of various humors descending from the head to the eyes and ears, and for excessive dreaming and toothache and sore throat, and especially for all illnesses that come from cold, such as paralysis and soda and apoplexy and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	 The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged with a dissolving medicine, cleansing the head three or four times, according to what the strength and nature and habit of the patient can endure; and then make the patient's head bald.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	 And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on a soft pillow; afterwards, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; and there where your fingers meet, bleed from there, then heat the cautery called "olivare", here is its form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And place it on the designated spot with ink, and in descending and squeezing your hand little by little while turning; then lift your hand immediately, and inspect the spot if you see a small bone; and if you do not see it, repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; afterwards, take a small amount of silk, and place soft cotton inside, and put on the spot, and leave for three days; afterwards, place a moistened cloth with butter; and leave it until the burn is healed; afterwards, treat the wound with an ointment called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	 And said the ancients, that when the wound remains open longer, it purges more; and therefore, it helps to move.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	 And some of these said that one should let the cautery burn until part of the bone is burnt, and then scrape away what has been burnt from the bone, and it should be treated.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	 And the others said that one should let the cautery burn so much, and push it in so hard that one cuts a piece of bone as wide as the spindle that women put in their distaffs, so that the humors may move out; and one must leave the wound open for a long time; afterwards, one must treat and heal it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	 And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be good at all, except in some men where there is a way for fear; and more it seems to me that I should leave it; because the head is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we testify in other members; and likewise when the head of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is more safe and gentle for me, and of this one I then work together with health. ️
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	 of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	 When there is chronic pain throughout the head and it lasts a long time, the patient should use yeris (herbs) and pills called "cochie", and purgatives for the head, and oils and plasters; and if one performs the cautery that we have previously mentioned and it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	 Take care that the patient's head is not of strong nature and is not too cold; then cauterize under that cautery a little, as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	 Then make a cautery above each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery in the place called "vasselz"; and it is the place where one puts cupping glasses; and lighten your hand so that you do not see down to the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere; and it is necessary that the cauteries of the horns be subtler than those used for the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	 Of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	 When pain suddenly occurs in one part of the head and the disease extends to the eye, and the head is purged by cleansing medicines, and other cures have been done as I have said in the division of diseases, and all this does not help: then he makes cauteries in two ways, that is to say with hot water and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	 The cautery with hot water is such that you take a pouch of garlic and remove the skin, then place it on the two temples, and then make an opening in the temple where the pain is located in such a way that you can put the garlic pouch under the skin; and when it is placed, tie it well and leave it like this for 12 hours; then untie it and draw out the garlic, and leave the wound like this for two or three days; then apply a cotton cloth soaked in butter until the flesh heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	 Après le cure d'oignement tant qu'il soit sané;
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	 Prends un cautere de fer et mets en la vouste,  et laisse le chauffer tant qu'il soit molt fort et ardant de grant feu;  et aprés ceo, tu auras un autre cautere de froid qui estoit ja devant chauffé.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	 Et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	 After, put cotton in vinegar water, and place it on the spot for three days; then put wet cotton in butter, and then treat the spot with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare," do so entirely at the point, and be careful not to cut the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	 of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	 When you treat migraine as we have said before in the division of illnesses, and it does not benefit, and you see that the cautery spoken of previously in medicine and iron does not help, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and similarly place it on the aching spot about half a line long, and remove your hand once, and hold so that you do not cut the artery and do not go as far as the bone; and beware of the jawbone which moves when one eats, and let the nerve have no regard for movement or spasm in the patient, and beware of excessive bleeding from the artery when it is cut, where cutting has great fear and especially for those who are not familiar with it and are not learned and experienced; and leave the work halfway; but I will tell you how to stop blood when an artery is cut, and I will show you in its place where it is needed in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	 And if you see that this cautery does not suit the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize in the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals; and if you wish, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better and more helpful than that one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	 of the pain in the ears due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	 When pain comes to the ear due to cold, and one has worked there with dissolving medicines and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pain does not move, then heat this cautery which is called "pointe", of which here is the shape:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After pricking all around the sick ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and move away a little above the root of the ear after you have signed the place of incision; and let there be ten points around each ear; then cure the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	 from the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	 Torment that must be cured by cautery is only of those that come from phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of illnesses; and do not make any cautery on those that come from dryness and contraction of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 When you cure this torment that comes from phlegm of ulcers and purgations of the head and gargling, and it does not work, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another a little in front of the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; and place the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and make a cautery toward the top of the ear slightly below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as a finger; and leave the cautery so long until half of the curve is burned; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And it is similar to the knife we placed before, but it is a little more delicate and the knife should be a little larger; after curing the place as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if the apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, and it does not improve, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, one in the place called "vasselz" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	 Of lead
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	 For this illness, it is necessary to give the patient large pears and brain-cleansing pills; after that, wash the entire head of the patient and apply on the back of the neck a mustard poultice as written in the treatise on poultices; and this is how to cauterize: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	 If he is healed in this way, it is good; and if not, let him make three cauteries in the middle of the head descending to the neck, and let there be two fingerbreadths between each cautery; and heal as with the others, and if you see it swell, and the patient can tolerate it, make one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two more on the two temples, and heal until it is healed; and let the cautery be called "olivare," as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	 of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	 It is necessary that the head be cleansed of hair and the things we have said before; after washing the patient's head, make a cautery in the middle of the head and on each temple, and one at the back and three on the nape of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient can tolerate it, and the illness is severe, make four cauteries on the nape of the back; and let it be as long as the most of the heart is burned, and lift your hand; after healing until it is healed, and let the cautery be called "olivare" that we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	 of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	 The epileptic should not use cautery except for the phlegmatic, and first one must temper the brain with years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is great and capable of taking medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, make him gargle and chew to temper the brain often with good food; after which raise his head in the middle, and there perform one cautery as we have said before, and a cautery on the vessel, and on each horn; and if the patient is strong and capable, then perform cauteries as I have said for someone who has paralysis and softness of the body, on the spine of the back and the neck, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	 If the patient is a child, perform a subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	 When due to melancholy there are excessive humors or corrupt moisture and thick phlegm, then cauterize with these subtle cauteries as we have said for those who have paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	 And if due to melancholy the excess is tending towards melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give him something to drink that will cleanse his brain, according to what was said earlier in the section on division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After washing the patient's head, make a linen bandage well made like a circle and place it in his head; let the patient sit cross-legged and be well held on all sides; then present the ointment, and use old goat butter; and heat it gently over a fire so that he can bear it when you apply it; afterwards empty the circle inside the head, and leave it to cool; do this for the patient every week once with another good treatment until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	 If you see someone being cauterized with many points throughout the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	 This manner of cautery softens the brain equally; and then place moistened cotton in butter and goose fat on top.
de l’awe des eulz	 from the moisture of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	 When moisture first comes to the eyes through the signs I mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient cleansing drinks, and guard against all moisture, and make him sweat in a bath several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	 After that, instruct the patient to shave their head, and make a cautery in the middle of the head, and make two cauteries on each of the two temples if the descent is in both eyes together, or one if the descent is in one; and cover all the veins and arteries under the skull with the cautery, and let the cautery be long according to the width of the temple; and guard against excessive bleeding, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it with as much power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	 And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision, the precaution on how to prevent it from bleeding; sometimes one cauterizes or burns under the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	 both bodies of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	 When the tears of the eyes are old and habitual, and are on the veins or near the arteries that appear on the outside of the head; and one sees that it is from cold superfluities phlegmatic, then he makes the cautery that I have said at the beginning of this chapter: a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries on each temple, and two cauteries under the two bones; and if there is more need, then he cauterizes wisely above the eyebrows with small cauteries.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	 dou corps des larmes par dedens les yeux
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	 Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	 Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	 Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare»;
de coi ci est li forme:	 de pourquoi cela se produit-il :
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if you see it this way, make two cauteries on the two sore spots as long as the sores are; and do not remove your hand until a third of the skin is burned, according to the method I have described.
dou poil qui point l’oil	 from hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	 Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes are turned inward and prick the eye, and then one makes cauteries according to two methods: by fire or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	 And for the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so that they do not move until they are born.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 When they are born and are equal, then place the patient in your health; afterwards make on the paper of the eyes a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs; then put moistened cotton soaked in egg white and musk-oil on the eye, then heat the cauterizing iron with this form.
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterwards cauterize on the figure that you have made little by little many times, so that the heart is burned in that place; and the sign of the health of the work is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs raised to the height of the eye; then remove your hand, and leave it thus for III days, then put moistened cotton in butter until the burn is removed; afterwards treat with ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	 And if after this the hairs come, and the skin is softened then renew the cautery on that same place, as you did first; and if the hairs are lacking, then cauterize so that the skin is raised to its natural place, and is equal, and the hairs do not prick the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	 The cautery of burning medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow until they are large and equal; then make a parchment form in the shape of a myrtle leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each one .З., and grind them together well; and do it quickly so that it does not cool; then spread it on the form you have made like the myrtle leaf, and place it on the skin of the eyes; and if the disease is in only one eye, then work on one, and if in both as well; and place moist cotton under the eye with egg white; and let the patient's eye be in your health and put your finger showing on the medicine, and press the bag and the egg every time the patient feels the bite of the medicine, for it bites like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	 When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medication from your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	 And when the bite has passed, lift the area with water, and inspect if you see the skin raised as if it had been raised by the constriction of fire or by incision; and if it is so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If not, then apply more medication to the area where the medicine has not worked, until your work is equal and your eyes are focused; then place moist cotton with butter on it until the scar has fallen off; after that, treat the area of the ointment, which is called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	 Et si tu as besoin de faire attention à ton travail avec grand soin, afin qu'aucune goutte de médicament n'entre dans les yeux.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	 Et si le papier devient mou par la suite, et les poils piquent dans l'œil, alors recommence l'application du médicament sur cette zone qui est assouplie par le papier proprement dit; continue ainsi jusqu'à ce que la plaie soit guérie. C'est ainsi qu'on utilise la feuille de myrte:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	 Et sachez que les yeux des hommes varient en taille et en petitesse, et selon cela doivent être vos contraintes; et il n'y a pas une seule méthode correcte pour ceux qui étudient cet art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	 Of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	 When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then it is necessary that you make cautery on it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	 Instruct the patient to put his head in your hand; and let the assistant hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or lower its head; then apply cotton soaked in egg white or parsley juice on the eye; then heat the cautery which is like this: and it is shaped at the top like the quill of a goose feather, together with which is the cautery; if you see, let it be pointed from one end to the other, and if you see, let it be like a tent; but nevertheless, this one which is shaped is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	 After pressing the fistula if it is open, drain the pus and dry it; and if it is closed, then work on it and draw out beyond the bone; afterwards place a very hot cautery, and hold your hand with the cautery at the part of the nose above the eye, so that your hand does not tremble; and put the cautery in the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	 If you reach the beginning of the cautery to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	 If not, then begin the cautery again once more, and another if you need it, and leave it for three days; afterwards apply cotton soaked in butter, and continue with drying ointment until it heals, and if forty days pass and it does not heal, then apply a corrosive medicine so that the bone is exposed; and the king according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	 Et il y a une manière de cautérisation pour la fistule que certains des anciens ont mentionnée.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	 And for the fistula, cut open the place; then put into the opening a thin camahan of which this is the form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	 and they make its quantity equal to a .З. of lead; and hold the camahan firmly in your hand, and the patient must not move at all, until the molten lead runs onto his eye; and one should put on the eye of the patient cotton moistened with egg white or honey: the lead thus heals the place of the fistula, and the healthy part by wonderful health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	 And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have spoken of, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	 If not, then it is necessary to administer perforations to the nose, and bring the fistula back into the body of the nose according to its own proper place.
des crevaices en levres	 holes in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	 Many times there are holes in the lips which are called "hair," and especially in children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	 When you treat these holes as we have said in sections, and the treatment does not help, then heat a small cautery knife according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And quickly insert it into these holes until it reaches the root; afterwards, treat the place with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	 of the abscess in the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	 When an abscess forms in the root of the throat or in the eye, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, and then it becomes putrid and foul-smelling and festers and turns into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in sections, and it does not help: then it is necessary that you have a cautery according to the size of the fistula; afterwards, open or perforate the hole of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the fire reaches the bottom of it, and in the deepest place; and do this once or twice, afterwards treat it as we have said in treatments, until it is healed; and if it is treated thus, it is good; and if not, then it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	 Of the movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	 When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicine but to no avail, then place the head of the patient in your lap; afterwards heat the cautery (the instrument) so that its form comes as follows: place a reed on the tooth; and put the hot cautery inside quickly; and hold your hand steady until the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; afterwards remove your hand and repeat the cautery according to your will; then the patient should fill their mouth with salt water, and keep it there for an hour and spit out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	 And in this way the tooth that was moving is firmly fixed, and the softened gum is restrained, and the moisture destroyed by drying.
de la dolor des dens	 of tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	 When tooth pain comes from cold, whether there is cold or wind, and medical treatments are ineffective, then a cautery is necessary according to two methods: a cautery with wax and a fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	 A wax cautery is such that you take cow's butter and put it on the tip of an iron or copper spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the end of a stick, soak it in melted butter, and place it quickly on the hurting tooth and hold it until it cools. And do this often until its power reaches the root of the tooth. And if you see, moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and place it on the hurting tooth, and put hot iron on it so that the heat reaches to the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	 The cautery with fire is such that you take a reed of iron or brass and make it thick enough so that the smoke does not reach the mouth of the patient; afterwards heat the cautery, from which the form will come later, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled down; do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And it is necessary for the patient to fill his mouth with good butter during the application of this cautery, and then rinse well; and that is the form of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	 And make a cautery from whatever tooth you wish, according to what you have the power to do; and that is the form of the reed.
des scrophules	 Of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When scrofula are caused by cold phlegm and moisture, and do not respond to digestion with medicines, then heat the cautery as specified below, and let it have two openings for the fumes to escape on the other side of the cautery; place the hot cautery on the abscess once or twice, depending on what is needed, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess; if the abscess is small, apply the cautery according to its size and leave it for three days; then place a cotton cloth soaked in butter over the burn until the blisters are removed; afterward, cure the area with onions and bindings until it heals.
Li forme de la cainne:	 The shape of the dog:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	 When the moisture overcomes the channels of the pomegranate, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient must first be emptied by purgative medicines; after that, make a cautery at the root of the throat, and take care not to reach the throat, and burn only a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then make another cautery at the junction of the neck with the top of the spine, and let the cautery be called "clavicle," as we have the form before; and treat the place as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	 for a cough
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	 When it is all about moisture and cold, and the patient does not have fever or dryness, and the disease is chronic, then make two cauteries on the chest in close places; and another cautery in the middle of the breast between two breasts; and let the cautery be called "clavicle" according to the form previously mentioned.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 And if you see, make a cautery by pricking at the entire area of the cautery which is called "pointe" in the case of the illness of the ears; and let there be pointee up to 30, or around that number.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	 After curing the place according to what was said before, and let the cautery be at three lines according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	 And because these cauteries are lighter, you should make them in three blows.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	 of the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	 When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reduce the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	 After let the patient lie on his back and on his side; then lift the heart which is within the tickling towards the two fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inside, heat the cautery which has two nerves as follows:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	 and cauterize the heart until it penetrates to the side, and the shape of the cautery should be accompanied by four other cauteries; and for this reason, the cautery is made with the three-nerve cautery, which is why the figures of the cauterization are six cauteries; and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the shape of the three-nerve cautery:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	 And sometimes it is positioned on this one nerve so that there are eight cauteries.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	 After, place the cautery upon the sore mixed with wax; afterwards, make the patient rest, and let the limb not be moved for a long time until it is well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 And if it is dislocated on top, which happens rarely, then make a cautery on the thick part of the cautery, or with many small cauteries.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 Because the joint is healed and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When cold and much moisture come into the stomach, so much that it harms his complexion, and many catarrhs occur to him, and in the usual manners of cures he does not benefit, then it is necessary that the patient be placed on his back, and stretch out his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 For this purpose, he makes three cauteries: one under the jawbone of the foot through the quantity of a finger, at all the cautery, claw-like; and two cauteries on the two sides so that the shape of the cauteries is at three angles, and has such space between each other that they are not joined together when they fall into decay; and let the cauteries be so deep that they pervade the two parts of the heart, and let the shape of the cauteries be according to this form without error:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form; and he who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and pressing on the stomach at one point according to the quantity that you see fit; then cauterize all the cautery which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Aprés le cure de la cure que nous avons eue devant, tant qu'il soit sain.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	 When the liver is in pain from cold and moisture and great flatulence, so much so that it has been moved out of its natural complexion by superfluities; and if the patient has been treated for this as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him at all, then the patient must be treated on his back; and make three cauteries according to this form and this figure and this quantity on the liver, outside the hypochondriac region, where the ribs of the man come together; and there should be a distance of one finger's width between each cautery; and the cauteries should be long in the body, and do not press your hand too much on the entire cautery; and only burn half of the head, and let the patient be upright on his feet; and if he cannot, then let him lie down, and stretch out his legs, and raise his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And if it is your will, then cauterize these cauteries of the scalpel, if you are skilled and knowledgeable in the art, and beware that you do not burn the entire heart, for you would dry out the whole body; and that it does not reach to boiling, for the heart is very sensitive there, as you should know.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 When there is an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain not very strongly; and if it is in the membrane, then he feels insane pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 And then when this cure should be done by the physicians, it is necessary that the patient lie on his back; and then sign the cross over the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which resembles a raisin, thus forming a cross.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 And he should be cauterized with a cautery until the heart is burned, and it comes up to the navel, so that all the putrefaction comes out; afterwards, treat him according to the treatment of burns until he is healed; and it is not necessary that anyone other than one who has long studied in the art of medicine use this cautery, for through whom many of these diseases have been cured.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Then he can safely work, and yet it seems to me that it is better to let him rest.
dou cautere de pleuresin	 of the cautery for pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	 The ancients said that for pleurisy one should make cauteries of the roots of aristolochia in this manner: take a long root of aristolochia, as large and as long as your fingers, and dry it, and moisten it in oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize with I cautery between the breastbone and the collarbone, and II small cauteries a little below in the part that is under the beard; and II cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining slightly behind; and I cautery in the middle of the chest, and I another on the stomach, and I between the two shoulders, and II on the sides of the chest opposite the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press your hand, but rather openly as when smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	 And some ancient ones say that some men use a cautery similar to a razor, and they heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches that abscess; and if the pain is severe, as we have said in the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	 But in this work, there is fear that the patient may die immediately, or a fistula may develop which cannot be healed.
de la mice	 of the flesh
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	 When you cure the disease of the flesh with what we have said in the division of cures, and it does not benefit at all, then there are three ways to use a cautery that are all good.
