The manner of the stitching is such that you gather the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or by thread, as I have made you know.
des apostemes des levres	 of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many people have hard abscesses within the lips, resembling grains of wheat, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, and cut above each knot, and take it with tweezers and cut into every part; then fill the place after the incision with crushed vitriol until the blood is darkened; and then the linen of ashes, and cure the place with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	 of the flesh of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	 Often a thick flesh grows on the gums, which the ancients call «albulus»; then you must hold it with tongs, and cut it at its root, and let the pus or blood flow out; then apply powdered vitriol or other restraining and desiccating powders to the place; and if that flesh returns after the incision, as often happens, then cut it a second time, and cauterize it: after cautery, it does not return; these are the forms of instruments for cutting.
des sordens	 from pus
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	 Sometimes there are scales at the roots of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and rough; and sometimes the teeth turn black and greenish yellow, so that the corruption spreads to the gum, and the teeth become foul-smelling; then you must have the patient sit between your hands, and his head in your lap, and scrape the teeth or scales until nothing remains; and do likewise for blackness and greenness and yellowing and other stains, until they are removed; and if at the first attempt it is not all removed, that is good; if not, then begin again on the second day and the third, until you have scraped everything away; and know that teeth require various forms of instruments for scraping, according to what the work demands, because the scrapers used for scraping outside the teeth have different shapes than those used between the teeth; and these shapes and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	 It is necessary that when you cure a tooth of its pain, you delay pulling it as long as possible, for one should not do this; because it is a very high substance until such time as there is no excuse to pull it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then when the patient is forced to have it pulled, it is necessary that you be certain of the aching tooth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Often the pain deceives the patient and he thinks it is in a healthy tooth, and has the good tooth pulled; but still the pain does not depart from this, until the evil tooth is removed, for we have seen this happen to those lords; and when you are certain of the aching tooth, it is necessary that you scrape around the tooth on all sides with a sharp instrument to protect the gum from all parts; then move it with your fingers or fine pliers little by little, until it is well loosened, then firmly clamp the pliers and let the patient’s head rest between your knees, and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extracting the tooth straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and lightly push it into each side, and remove it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is perforated and decayed, then it is necessary that you fill it with rags where the holes are; and gently take hold of it with the tongs so as not to break it when pulling; and it is very important to work carefully around the gum to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And take good care that you do not break it, and leave a part behind, and the patient will have greater pain from the root than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And beware not to act as the ignorant surgeons do, who sometimes break the jawbone due to their haste and boldness, and do not bring what we have mentioned; but sometimes cause great illness due to the roots that remain or the broken jawbone, as we often see. When the tooth is extracted, wash the place with wine or vinegar and salt; and if blood continues to flow there, which often happens, fill the place with burnt vitriol; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	 The forms of the instruments, with which one removes teeth first, should have long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	 And let them be of thick members, so that they do not bend when pulling, and let them be well-made iron, and let them be toothed for a firm grip.
de la racine des dens	 from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	 When the root remains after pulling, then you must place cotton soaked in butter on the spot for one or two days.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	 until the spot is softened, then apply the pincers called "algefri", which resemble a bird's beak; and let them be made inside like a file, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if the roots do not want to come out with these tweezers, then you must uncover all the flesh around the root, and place there the instrument called "althali," that is to say, pincers, of which here is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	 And let it be thin and large so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out with this, it is good; if not, then help yourself with all the instruments, of which the forms come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	 And one helps oneself with this instrument that has two blades, of which here is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	 and other iron tools that are in front of the teeth, and this instrument that looks like large tweezers, of which here is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	 And let this instrument be such that it cannot break; and know that there are many dental instruments; and so with other instruments, which are not counted; and the wise master finds his own instrument by himself, according to what his work and the disease show him, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach any instrument because of their diversity; and if one breaks a bone or others, then he looks for the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, which is thus formed:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	 And let them be large and well-holding to hold the bone so that it does not escape, but can hold and remove it; and then restore the place with suitable medicines for this, and if there is decay in the bone and it is small, then he extracts it all with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	 When the teeth appear not according to natural form, and their shape is unsightly, especially in young women, you should know if the tooth is new after another tooth, and is not in its rightful place, and it cannot be filed or ground down; then extract it. And if it is too close to the adjacent tooth, take this instrument whose shape is like a small beak and is made of iron, sharp at the end.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	 And the instrument cuts little by little each day due to the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others; and if it is accessible, such that it can be filed, then file it with a file like this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	 and it is also like the file used to make needles; and with this file, gently file the tooth little by little each day, so that it does not move until it falls out; then smooth it in the end with any rasp, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, it must be filed down until it is even, so that it no longer cuts the tongue nor corrupts speech.
quant li dent lochent	 when the tooth moves
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 when the front tooth moves, either by impact or falling, and the patient cannot bite on what they are eating without it falling out, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines, and that does not work; then they must be restrained with a gold thread, for the silver thread turns green and rots, but the gold never moves; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin nor too small, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you want to straighten the teeth, take the thread and fold it double between the two healthy teeth, then put the knot between the loose teeth, one or more, as long as you can wisely reach up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then start covering again until the place where you began, and gently and wisely tighten your hand so that it does not move; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then cut the ends of the wire with pliers, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy teeth, and put them in such a way that they do not hurt the tongue; and then leave it so tight as long as it can stay, and if it comes loose or the wire breaks, hold it with another wire; thus it will remain and serve for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	 And when the tooth falls out, put it back in its place, fresh by fresh, as we have said; and do not interfere with this unless you are wise and patient, and sometimes a form is made from a cow's bone, and it is placed where the lack is, and it is held as we have said, and remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	 to cut the tendon of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Never is this tendon which comes from under the tongue by nature, that one is born thus; or by accident of a healed wound; and the work is such that you open the patient's mouth and hold their head in your hands, and lift up the tongue; then cut the nervous tendon wide, so that the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and this is from a sudden wound, then insert the hook and cut wide that tendon; and beware that the slit is not too deep, for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done this, lift up the place with rose water and aloes, or cold water, then put under the tongue a linen bandage; and the patient should change the bandage every night, so that the place cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 And if bleeding follows, apply vitriol ointment to the spot; and if the blood does not stop, cauterize with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this; then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it as the color of pitch or black or hard so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is cancer; and if it inclines towards yellowish, and there is moisture, apply alum, and make a fine incision with a scalpel, and cleanse it from both sides; and if the blood does not stop at your work, apply vitriol ointment until it is dried, then return to your work until you have drawn out all the pus; then lift up the spot with soft cloths, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	 From the abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 Any time there are sores inside the throat called "godath," which are properly known as the two almonds; and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is a hard abscess of small sense and of fox color, then do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also to avoid bleeding; but leave it until it dies, and then you will cut it, or it would burst by itself; and if it is of white color again, and the root is subtle, have the instrument prepared for cutting, but first check if the abscess is warm and settled.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	 Then make the patient sit before the sun, and let his eyes be in your shadow, and have him open his mouth and take the instrument between his hands, and press the tongue down with all the tool, which is here the shape; and it should be of silver or fine copper like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	 When you press the tongue with all this tool, and you see the abscess, then take the onion and fix it in the almond, and draw it strongly above as much as you can; and draw something from the cloths with it, then cut with the instrument, which is here the shape, which looks like a forceps; and nevertheless the heads are curved, and one after another, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	 And if you do not have this instrument, then rent it from the tongs, which is of this form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	 And let it be sharp on one side and smooth on the other; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, then cut the other in the same manner, and afterwards gargle the patient with hot water and warm water, and if there is a flow of blood, then gargle the patient with water in which pomegranate peels or myrtle leaves have been cooked, and similar things, until the wound is stanched; then bandage it until it heals; and sometimes other abscesses arise in the throat in addition to the two tonsils, so cut them also in the same way as the two tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman for an abscess that was born within the throat, that is to say, a small abscess; and it had nearly closed off the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the blocked passage, nor could she eat or drink, and would have died if she remained thus for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess was so swollen that it had forced out two veins through the two passages of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 I hastened immediately and inserted a needle into one [of the passages], then drew it out, and removed a large portion of pus; then I repeated the same in the other nostril, and opened her mouth and pressed her tongue; afterwards I inserted the needle into these abscesses, and emptied some of it, but only a little blood came out; and thus the passage of the woman's throat was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not cease cutting this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again immediately, and filled the place that I had emptied, so much so that it became very large; then I cauterized it inside the throat: thus it remained without growing; and I left these parts, and only God knows what became of her after me.
de l’uve	 of the grape
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When the grape descends into the urethra and is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below and large and round, it is called "grape".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	 When it is cut in the way we have said in the division, and the cutting does not benefit at all, and you see that the abscess is calmed down, and it is subtle, then you must stop; and that which is round and gathered together and is not long; and it is bloody or of the color of the rind or black, then you must avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	 For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	 Therefore, when you see it according to the manner that I have said, of its whiteness and its length, you must make the patient sit before the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument that we have remembered before; then insert the probe into the urethra, and draw it down, and cut it with one of the two instruments that I have said in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And it is necessary that you not cut more than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; for if you cut more, it injures the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the II amandres, and care for it until it heals.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	 And if the patient is afraid of being cut, then you must use ingenuity in order to perform the cautery without causing fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	 And the manner of the cautery should be sharp and keen.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	 And the patient should place his head in your hand, and then press the tongue against the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter on cautery, and apply with a sharp, lively knife, so that it is not too thick nor too thin; and use the handle of this instrument, which has this shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And on the head, there should be a hair or something where one puts the medicine, like the hairs of a spoon, and put the instrument with all the medicine on the eye; and the patient should lie on their side, so that the saliva and mucus run from their mouth into the medicine, so that it does not go down to the throat and wound; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the eye, for an amount of time equal to half an hour, until you see it darkened and the stings of the medicine are soothed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument with all the cotton into the canal above, until the cotton dries on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is perfected, then let it dry, and after four days or five it will fall off. And if you need to restart the cautery of the medicine, start again, and after the cautery wipe around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and treat with gargles until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	 This cure is more suitable for incision than for cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner, take calamint and hyssop and origanum and rue and chamomile and arnica and similar herbs, and assemble them all or some of them in a pot, and put ashes in it, and boil; and let the pot be well sealed with strong clay, and in the middle of the pot let there be an implement made according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	 And let it be of silver or bronze, and let one of the ends be thrust into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, so that the eye may be smoked; after that, repeat often, until the eye dries out, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the appearance of a hot abscess, for many things happen then; and do not do it except at the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	 And if this instrument is not present, then take a reed and place inside the chief a clove of garlic, so that the mouth of the patient does not become too hot; for the garlic clove does not let the vapor bother the mouth, and this is a good cure along with healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	 Often a bone or fish spine gets stuck in the throat, or something else; so you must remove what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see the thing move; and what does not open and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit before the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the hard thing will come out with the vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of wool, or a lettuce root, or a crumb of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge, and then swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will swell, and then you will pull it out strongly; and if it does not come out with what we have said, then take an instrument of lead according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	 And let the instrument be bent at the end so that it can enter more easily into the throat, and have the head raised up high; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, lest it should swell or the bone may go in; and it is better that the patient pushes the instrument, because it is difficult for him to do so; thus he pushes downwards where he draws it out strongly with all of the instrument equally, until it comes out.
de la sansue de la gorge	 of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Sometimes the blood is treated by medicines, as I have said in the division, through the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help at all, then look into the throat of the patient towards the sun, after you press the tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see blood, then draw it out with the smallest hook or with subtle pincers that serve for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if this does not work, take a hollow reed and insert it into the patient's throat, then insert a hot iron into the end of the reed, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And if the patient has diarrhea all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 then take a full vessel of cold water and open the mouth and pour it in without gagging and move it with their hand often; and as soon as the blood senses the water, it will fall out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafoetida using the instrument I mentioned for eye fumigation; do this many times, for it will fall without delay.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 And the manner of fumigation is thus: you take a pot in which there are live coals, and let it be covered with a cloth pierced in the middle, and through that hole place the head of the instrument; then cast your fumigation, and the patient places the end of the cane in his mouth, and closes his mouth so that no smoke escapes, but rather reaches the blood vessels; and the blood will now fall out, and if it does not fall out, repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient bear thirst, and eat salty things and the like, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for it to flow out by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	 And the form of the instrument with which one draws blood is such that, when it can be seen, it resembles curved pincers to enter into the throat; and let it have a similarity to a hawk's beak, and let there be roughness like a file, so that what it takes, it cannot leave behind; and see here its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	 the chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 There are many kinds of abscesses, according to what comes to mind next in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision; and it is in two manners: one is in its very appearance, and those that retain moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second manner is according to the places where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For the boils on the head are different from those at the base, and the boils on fleshy places are different from those that appear in joints, and each one should be judged according to its work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And there are boils that should not be punctured until the head is ripe according to its maturity; and there are such that must be punctured when they are hardened, and do not mature according to their nature, as with boils near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 For when boils occur near joints and are left until they are ripened around them, sometimes the ligaments and nerves of the joint are corrupted, which causes contracture in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 Or if the boil is near a main joint and you delay the puncture until it is ripe, it will harm the main joint; but if it is at the base, then perforate it before it is ripe; and it is not necessary to pierce hardened boils whose digestion is not complete, except for those at the base, lest they become deep-seated and form a fistula within, which cannot heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	 Et covient que tu saiches l'heure de la perforation de l'aposteme qui est mûre selon l'accomplissement, et c'est quand la douleur est apaisée, et le départ des fièvres, et l'amenuisement de la douleur et de la rougeur, et du débatement et de l'aggravation du chef de l'aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu fasses seoir la perforation ou plus dépendant leu de l'aposteme, et là où il apert mues; et soit la perforation douce du corps, et s'il y a des apostèmes aux mains ou aux pieds, ou dans les articulations et au nerfs et aux artères, et en tous lieux égaux où il n'y a point de pliure.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In those that bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 And when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you let the perforation remain until it is confirmed by complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it before that, the body will be filled with poison from it, and it will be full of much filth; and by chance the edges and depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And if any abscess is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	 And it is necessary that you bring in small abscesses, small holes; and in large abscesses, large holes, and many cuts according to the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to remove the core, and cover when they have become as thin as cloths, and are dead, then you should do as with buboes: and there are those which are cut into three corners, and there are those from which one cuts like the leaves of myrtle, as abscesses of the anus; and there are those where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar cuts.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	 Those who have no head, as in a soft superficial abscess, you must pierce it completely; and when the abscess is large and has drawn much pus, if you pierce it, do not draw all the pus in that hour, but only some of it; then pack the abscess with lint until the next day, then drain it again; repeat this many times from large to small, until all the pus is drawn out; similarly if the patient is weak or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old and infirm man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the spirit leaps sometimes with the release of pus, which may cause the patient to die, and you might not notice it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Avoid this chapter with great care, and when you have perceived your abscess, clean the wound, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a simple cut, then bring in ten linen or old cotton swabs; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many openings, then it is necessary that you insert one into each opening so that they touch each other; and if you have cut into the abscess some of the skin, and you have removed it, then it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or shavings of linen without moisture, and bind it until the third day; then remove it, and treat it with oil until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 And if there is continuous bleeding during your work, bring cold and fresh water, and soak the cloth, and place it on the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the bleeding persists, bring management and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned earlier in this book, and if it is in winter, and the area of the abscess is very nervous, then you must place hot wine and oil-soaked tents and cloths; and if it is in summer, and the area is fleshy, then you must place cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, for three days, as we have said; and then lance the abscess and dry and treat it, as needed, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	 And this must be recognized generally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed in the treatment of abscesses, and see here the chapter.
des soros	 of boils
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	 Where the head has small abscesses, and they are similar to those that are in fabrics, like the embroidery of a pillowcase, and there are many such examples.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	 Some are fatty and of such where there is moisture like a pustule; and there are those which are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the surgeon does not do otherwise.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	 And the work of cutting is such that you try with any instrument called "trocar," from which the shape comes afterwards, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	 Because if it contains moisture, then split it open along its length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	 And when the moisture is emptied, then scrape off without leaving any skin that contains this moisture, for it always returns if anything remains there; then soak cotton in Egyptian ointment, if available; if not, in water and oil, and fill the wound with it, and leave it until the next day; and these will heal those who remain of the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And then renew the cotton, as before, on the second day and the third, until you are sure that there is no more of the night left; then treat the wound with an appropriate ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	 And if the abscess holds a lot of pus, cut it according to this form, lengthwise; and throw away your nails, and scrape from all sides, and put all your care into drawing out the skin in which it lies; and if the artery gives you trouble, then do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	 And do the same for the abscess if it is pious, and in cutting and healing as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	 And cut above the pious and moist abscess, for it is lighter, because they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	 And if some of these abscesses have no moisture at the head, like those abscesses that I cut from the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a stone, rough and white, and it could not be broken; and if one had struck it, they would have caused a wound just as with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	 In other abscesses coming to the head, except for those which come to the heads of children and the roots of the ears, let the opening always be in the most dependent place, so that the pus may exit; and treat them as needed.
des scrophules	 of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	 Often these abscesses occur on the neck and under the armpits and in the groin, and sometimes they appear elsewhere in the body, and they are many and interconnected with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	 And each scrofula is properly inside its own rib, as the knot and the head abscess are, as we have said; and there are many similarities among these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	 There are some that contain moisture, and there are also some that are malignant and do not want to obey healthfulness.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	 In that case where you see a good arrangement for touching, and it is similar to the color of the body, and it moves from every part and is not harsh on the nerves of the neck or on the artery or on the conduit, and it is not deep; then you must cut above it, and scrape each part, and extend the two lips of the heart to the corners, if you need them, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and draw little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and let the knife not be too sharp or cutting, which the hand may slip, and do not move forward too much, so that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	 And if you cut the vein or artery and it does not stop bleeding, then put in the wound vitriol powder, or any powders that staunch blood, and compress the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed, and the wound softens, and begins to suppurate.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	 And when the blood is staunched, return to your work until you complete it; then see if there remain any small scabs, cut and clean them away.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	 And if there is a large vein in the root of the scab, it should not be cut at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it fall off by itself without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	 And if you cut off the entire scrofula, it is necessary that you join together the two lips of the wound and sew them now, since there is no excess due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	 it is necessary that you understand how to cut at the root of it and pull strongly, and sew as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Those scrofulae that have excess, pierce there where it is more open; and pierce as the one mentioned before, hanging downward, then bring tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with ointment of fresh meat, until it is healed. ię It is necessary to know how to cut at the root of the scrofula and pull strongly, and sew as we have said.
de squinance	 Of scurf
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	 The ancients spoke and talked about the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen anyone in our land who did it, and this is written from their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	 For those who have scurf, it is necessary that the cleft of the throat called "epiglottis" be cut; and one should not help with this, because all the veins and the spleen of the patient are hot in those who have an abscess in the mouth or throat or both tonsils.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	 When the disease is in the duct of the spleen, it is necessary to cut the epiglottis to avoid death from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	 Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we should make a small cut across it, between the II and III cartilages or according to the size of the incision of the trachea, not in the cartilage; and this place is suitable for the section of the epiglottis because there is no flesh there, and the vessels are long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	 And if the master is afraid, it is necessary that he extend the skin of the throat to the entire neck, then split the heart until it reaches the chin; and avoid the vessels of blood, if you see any; and then cut off the spleen as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the phlegm from the chin which jumps forth through the place that is broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the hour has passed in which strangulation is feared, gather together the two lips of the heart wound, and sew it up alone without a bandage; then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	 Albucasim said that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the fault is on him.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	 Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and therefore the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the illness of the disease has passed, which passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, until it was cured; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	 I saw that a young lady took a knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the veins of the lung; and I was called to cure her, and found her almost dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	 I uncovered the wound, and found the blood that had come out of it, and although it had not cut a vein or artery except for the throat, the air was coming out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	 I hastened, and sewed up the wound, and treated it until it was healed; and it happened to the maiden that she lost her voice, but afterwards she returned to her normal condition; therefore I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	 of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	 This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat," and it is a great abscess in color like a blackbird, and it is very common in women; and there are two kinds: natural, and accidental; in the natural kind there is no gland.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 And the incident is according to II manners, of which one is similar to fat us, and the other manner is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it should not be worked on by making incisions except in that which is small, and test and search all around: if you find it thus as I know fat, and does not open into any vein, then strike it, as one strikes a nose, and pull out all its hair, if there is any; and examine well soon, and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	 of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	 Many manners of us are, of which I will say all the likenesses; and now it is necessary that I say all the difference that is between us and issuing forth.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	 Je dis que la dislocation survient en cas de fièvre continue, jusqu'à ce que l'inflammation soit passée et que la pourriture soit complète; alors la fièvre et la chaleur s'apaisent.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	 Avec le nouveau, il n'y a ni chaleur, ni fièvre, ni douleur, et l'on trouve le syfac, qui est son propre sac et correspond à la couleur du corps, et commence comme une petite poche, puis grossit; et il y en a deux sortes, soit graisseux, soit humides, et beaucoup de couleurs sont comme je l'ai dit dans la division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	 Il faut, lorsque tu viens à la cure du nouveau, que tu examines d'abord et enquêtes de tous les instruments appelés "entromissoire", selon la forme que vous verrez dans le chapitre suivant.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	 And the manner of inquiring about abscesses from us is that you take the moistest place you find in the abscess, and turn your fingers a little at a time, so that you know that the instrument has reached the heart of it; then according to the size of the abscess, afterwards remove the obstructive device, and be careful not to make it jump out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	 If the running moisture has color, open it as I have said of other abscesses; and if after the obstructive device comes more moisture, know that it is greasy, then open it in a cross shape, and take it with pincers, and lightly scrape each part and ward off the skin where it lies so that you draw it out whole with the knot; and if you cannot draw it out whole, then draw it out piece by piece so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	 Car if something remains there, the nose returns many times; and if a little bit remains, and the flesh is troubled by it, then fill the wound with some corrosive powders, and close the wound, and apply soothing things to the hot abscess, and perform other cures until healed; and if the nose is large, then sew together the two lips of the wound, and cure that which injures the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	 And if the pulsating vein is against you or another, then hasten and fill the place with crushed vitriol, and leave it for two days or three, until the wound putrefies, and the blood's ebullition rests; then return to cut out that which remains of the knot.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	 Here are the forms of the instruments for cautery, and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret," and one which is called "breb," and they are also of three kinds: large, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistula; and they are like the needles with which one sews sorcerers' caps, and they are made of yellow brass, or iron, or silver, and those which are yellow are worth more, and they are tried with black lead to surround the edges of fistula; and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the width of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	 The forms of the nails are of many kinds, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are nails that have two curves in three ways likewise; and there are nails that have three curves, and they are also of three types; and there are nails that have two curves, and single-curved nails, and they are also of three types; and all these are necessary for their purpose.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	 The heads of these instruments are sharp, and there are some that cut only from one side, with which one can peel the fingers so as not to cut the vein or nerve; and among these introducers are the reamers that are enclosed in sleeves, so that the patient does not perceive them when opening abscesses; and they come in three sizes: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses them only in fleshy places, such as legs, arms, breasts, and joints, and similar places; and sometimes one makes another small instrument, resembling splinters of wood, according to this form, with which one stanches blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	 And one places it sometimes at the place that heals quickly with cutting of veins, and of arteries, and sometimes they return according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	 Sometimes the breasts of certain men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so much so that they resemble women's breasts; and they remain unsightly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, must proceed according to this form from this line .b. until .g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	 Then peel off the fat, and fill the wound with medicine made from flesh, then join the two lips of the wound together with stitches, and cure it until it is healed; and if the breast hangs down and is softened by its size as happens to women, then cut it into two ribs above, through two similar slits; so that one slit adheres to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the longer line contains the shorter according to this form, from this line .b. until this line .g.; then peel off the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about stitches and powders, and whatever is necessary for the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the flow of blood, then you must fill the wound with soaked cotton in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it consumes the remaining fat and skin, then cure it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	 of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	 These abscesses that come under the armpits are types of hard scrofula where there are ribs, and some contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	 Therefore, those that contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line b to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been drained, fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton, and treat with an appropriate ointment until it heals.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if the abscess is like scrofula, then cut it as we have said for cutting scrofula, and if the wound releases pus, then apply a caustic as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	 Of the tearing of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	 When the artery is torn and the skin above it is stitched together, there are often abscesses, and the same happens with an inflamed vein and abscess; and one can tell if it is due to the artery because the abscess is long and deep; and when you touch it with your fingers, you feel a tightness; and when it is due to the vein, there is a red appearance on the outside; and it is foolish to lance this abscess, especially when it is under the nails and in the corners and in the neck and in many other places, and it is very large.
