Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find a rottenness in the skin and it is not on the bone, then cut off all the rottenness, and throw it away, then cure it; and if there is a vein or artery in the wound that does not stop bleeding with medicine, then seek the vein or artery, and if you find it dislocated, then bind it with a thread; and if this does not help at all, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	 And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and it is that you place in this powder which seals before the fire has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and make it into a fine powder, and fill the wound, and bind it strongly, until it heals well and joins with all its blood; and then bind it well, and leave it unbound, if it does not swell; for one does not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	 And sometimes one does this with quicklime alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but the fire must have moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound has moved, even if it was there, do not put any of this powder on it; but apply some cooked onions, or paste made of barley flour with water and honey, until it heals; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine tweezers; and I will tell you hereafter about fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	 of a neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	 If the wound is in the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between it and one of the head, but if a nerve of the neck or an artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is the nerve, there is no other device than to let the cure be, and not to put anything restraining on it, for it harms the nerves and makes them recede; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be lukewarm, like warm water mixed with rose oil, and washed in the same manner, and other stones of small size according to this method, and moist compresses.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound is large, then stitch and bind it with bandages, and let it heal.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and hollow and full of pus, then pierce it in a lower place; and if an artery is cut, and the flow of blood continues, then desiccate it, let it bleed, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the esophagus or the heart is cut, and the pathway is preserved so that food can pass, then sew the heart onto the spinal cord of the neck, and do not touch the neck but restore it according to its natural shape; and then bind it appropriately, and leave it for some days, then cure it with drying compresses until it heals; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then hollow it out; and if there are pieces of bone, then draw them all out if you can, and those that you cannot have, then leave it until the wound putsrefies, and the issue is dry and clean; and if the wound is fresh, then sprinkle the powder I mentioned onto it.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	 And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	 of the lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, observe if there are bubbles coming out of the wound as the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it in the first hour, nor bind it for the blood to flow deeply and return to the heart, killing the patient; but apply astringent ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you do not have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb excess moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; then there will be no spasm, no heart tremor, nor difficulty breathing; and when you see good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Cure it then with bandages and other treatments until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, work, always know that there is a fistula; treat it as necessary.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And if the wound is from the incision of a sword or knife, and it is simple, whether on the back or in front, treat it with what is before it; if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is close to the bone and has struck pieces, cleanse the wound, and draw out the bones if they are exposed; and if they are not exposed, leave the wound to fester, which will ease extraction; and for other wounds on other limbs, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	 Of the bursting of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The bursting of the belly is great and medium and small; of the large wound sometimes escapes the intestine, or the nerve of the intestines, causing their obstruction; and the suture is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because it is harder to put the intestines back in if they are not replaced immediately; because the intestines swell quickly when they feel the cold, and it is harder for them to go back in, and that's why the medium-sized wound is better, because it is easier to replace the intestine than in others. And know that the suture of the belly follows three types: two common sutures occur in the suture of the belly, and the suture of other wounds of the body; and two other specific sutures are common to other wounds; and nevertheless, they are more specific with the suture of the belly, and I will say each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 Je dis que quand la blessure est petite et que quelque chose de l'intestin en sort, c'est une chose grave à réparer, cela se fait par l'une des deux manières : soit à cause de la petitesse de la blessure, comme nous avons dit, soit parce que l'intestin est gonflé par le froid.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 Et quand il est froid, réchauffez-le de cette manière : mouillez une éponge ou un petit drap dans de l'eau tiède seulement, ou faites cuire du vin avec des épices et du poivre, puis arrosez l'intestin jusqu'à ce que le gonflement disparaisse ; parfois, ce vin a un effet resserrant.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the inflammation subside, soften the intestines with hot water or ale and mallows that have been cooked, for thus is the entrance made easy at a little thing; and if it cannot enter, make a small opening in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is to move so that it cuts, for no one should cut there without great necessity; and this is the instrument to split: cut inside on the curve and not outside, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is widened, and the intestine protrudes outside, put it back in its natural form in its proper place, if you can, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, you must have the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the belly, then put the head and the breast higher than the parts below, and likewise if the tear of the belly is in one of the two parts, focus so that the injured part is higher than the other; and thus you must administer as I say for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 In small wounds use what you have prepared, then have in your hands a pious assistant who holds the entire tear at his hand, and gathers the lips; and this is the common manner of stitching, and it is that you take one needle or more according to the width of the wound, then leave two finger-widths from the head of the wound, and insert a needle where there is a good strong thread; and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the siphac, which is under the skin inside, so that you make it pierce from that side, and gather the two heads of the siphac together four at a time; then strain a double thread around the needle on both sides, then gather the two lips of the wound together, then leave two finger-widths, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you did the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you need for the needles, until the entire wound is restrained; and let the needles be moderate, between fine and thick, because fine needles cut all the flesh, and those that are too thick cannot enter well: therefore they must be moderate; and it is not necessary to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they cut and work the wound before the suturing; and then cut the heads of the needles, so that they do not hurt the patient while sleeping, and put tents or bandages on the heads of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this manner of stitching with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because one can insert one or two needles in the second suturing, which is common, and it is that you gather the two heads of the skin and the two heads of the siphac together with a needle where there is a medium strong thread; and when you have pierced these four heads together, then remove the needle to the part where you began, in the manner as one sews clothes; and put space between each suturing the thickness of a small finger; this stitching is known by men, and I sewed a wound that a man had in the belly, who was wounded by a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and the intestines protruded well two palms wide, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I returned his intestines after they had been outside for twenty-four hours, and the wound was closed for fifteen days, and I cared for it, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in place I where none were found, nor any medicines; and I put old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and pass it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced the skin straight on straight, leave the head of the silk or thread where you passed the needle, and make it pierce again from the inside to the outside; and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew as the furriers do with furs, and that you leave the thread once on one side, and take it up again on the other, until the stitching is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galiens thus spoke these words, and some testify to this, that one must sew the belly with two needles, each having a thread; and one should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who sew straps; and know that when the stitching is in the middle of the belly, it causes more pain than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and this is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, before the fire has touched it, then resume the cauterization of the intestines, and the wound; then place a healing powder on top, and if the fire has touched it, then apply some ointment that is available, until the wound heals; and stitch the threads, and let the sifac and mirach be sealed; then cure the wound as others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then apply, as soon as it begins to drip pus, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 For in many situations when the wounds are simple, you have no need of other medicines; and if you doubt that the wound will affect the main members, then it is necessary for you to moisten a light linen cloth in warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the angles and under the armpits; and if there is pain or rotting in the belly, which often happens, clisterize with tepid black wine, and also if the rotting goes as far as the intestines; pierce them from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine that is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is injured, and this is due to the thinness of its walls, and the delicacy of the entire body, and the closeness of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the intestine protrudes from the wound, put it back as you would with the intestines, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has turned green or black, then you must tie off the blackened area so that blood does not flow there, for there are veins and arteries; then cut the part between the ligature, and hang the two ends from the underside of the wound down to prevent tugging when the intestine falls back, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	 of the bladder's rupture
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, for I saw a man wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became festering and turned into a fistula, from which excrement and flatulence issued forth; I applied treatment as best I could, and did not cease to be diligent until he was healed, and the place sealed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it sewn, I feared that the patient had an illness in his stomach; but there was no illness, rather he remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner: take large-headed clips, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the clip has opened its mouth, place it over the two lips so that it pulls its mouth shut; and then strike its head, and it stays in such a way that it cannot untie itself, then place another clip afterwards in the same manner as before, until the entire wound is seized; and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 This chief if embeds in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a manner: take the end of this intestinal thread that is very thin, and then tie to the end of this thread a fine twisted linen thread, then put the thread through the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it together; and this manner of suturing is not beyond the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is great and wide, especially when it is in one of the large intestines, there is no skill or wisdom, except for finesse.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	 of a fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 Know that any wound or abscess, when it heals, is universally called a "fistula," especially when it is healed and closes inward.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And according to the truth, a fistula is a hard and white scar that does not cause pain, and it closes like the feather of a bird; sometimes it closes clearly thinly, other times thickly; sometimes hollow, other times enough; and I have already spoken about this in the division of wounds, that every wound that does not heal, and there is no flesh there, it is only open due to one of the NINE causes: namely, due to the scarcity of blood or body; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh within, and on the lips, which prevents flesh from growing; or there is too much swelling; or the place is rotten, and the material is of poor quality; or the medicine used for treatment is not good; or because the corruption is of a pestilential nature; or due to the property in the region where digestion is slow, and healing is delayed, and it is swollen by nature; or there are veins or bones present: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	 Or it is necessary that I inform you of the treatment for a fistula made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that fistulas occur in all members of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or from the sinuses, or intestines, or bladder, or some of the ribs, or spine of the back, or any joints of the hands or feet; and also such that comes to the property of the principal member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all the fistulas that are of this manner are of grave difficulty and there is nothing but work and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you recognize it, then take a probe of bronze or iron, if the fistula is straight, seek it out; and if the fistula is crooked, seek it out with a subtle probe of boxwood, for boxwood bends more easily around the curvature; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot probe it well with probes, then irrigate it through one of the openings, for moisture passes from one opening to another, and cleans it; then seek it out wisely as best you can, so that you may know if there is bone or nerve, and cut deeply until you reach it, and inquire carefully from the patient about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and the place where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or in any of the places I have told you, then cut according to what I have said, and remove the foul smell and corrupt matter that are inside; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep in a straight place, then you must cut deeply as much as you can, then put moist dressings in astringent medicine, and push them up to the top of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess matter that remains at the bottom; and then put on bandages with healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it does not heal this way, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then cut it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If a vein or nerve is injured in the main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is decay and blackness, then scrape it until all the decay is removed, then treat the wounds with meat until they are healed; and if they are not healed, and the wound reopens as before, know that you have not reached the bottom: reveal and seek until you are at the bottom, remove all the decay, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If not, know that the decay is too deep for you to reach it; there is no other remedy than to leave it to nature. And if there is a small piece of rotten bone, and you can extract it with pincers, then draw it out with an appropriate instrument. And if there are many bones, draw them all out, leaving not one; and if moisture prevents you, and there is no mistake or fear, cut and moisten and cover the flesh, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove them within an hour, then place on the wound something that causes rotting, and let it rot around the bones until the flesh is completely rotten; and then the bones will be more easily removed. If it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, then wait only for the rotting to remove all the blackness, then close the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption and it reaches the marrow of the bone; then you must saw and cut up to the corruption, and then heal it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 It was a young man about thirty years old who had pain in his leg from an internal cause that entered the body, so much so that the matter came to the leg and it swelled with a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it; but the doctors in their foolishness worked on it until the abscess opened, and they let out a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and through it came a lot of openings that all threw out pus and moisture from the body; and many doctors attended to him for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine, until I was called upon, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was being treated, and what was coming out through the openings in great quantity; and the young man's body was turning red, and had a citrine color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 Je placed a tent in one of these openings, and then I searched all the openings, and I found that one comes against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 I hurried then, and cut into one of the openings until I exposed a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the rot reached all the way to the inside of the bone; I removed what appeared to me of the rotten bone, and thought there was no other rot except that which I removed; and I began to treat the wound with healing medicines for a long time, but it would not heal; and then I tried again, and exposed the bone as before, and found the rot continuing in the bone, and removed it, and then worked on healing the place; but I could not do so until I cut around a palm's width of the bone, and drew it out completely, and then treated it with medicines; and it healed and closed quickly, and I did not need to start the work again except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear it, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 Car for the evacuation he often bled, but he was completely cured, and in place of the bone a hard flesh grew, and it was well-formed and had no harm or contrary effect at all, neither coming nor going.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be set in this manner: take a cord and tie it to the end of the broken bone that is protruding, and command someone to pull it upward; and put another thicker cloth cord above the first cord, and tie it on the flesh that is over the bone, and stretch the end, so that you draw the corrupted flesh out from below, and expose the flesh in the place where you wish to set the bone, so that the string does not cut the flesh; and put a piece of wood or a board under the bone to help press down the corrupted flesh; and it should be set as much as can be seen and felt the corruption, and set again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, and place a piece of wood underneath; puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, and saw from one part to the other through the corruption; et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; and let the sawing continue along the length of the corruption as we have said; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, if the corruption is in the joint; si cope la jointure corrumpue, and cut the corrupt joint; et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; and saw the bone where it contains the other part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints; si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; there is no other remedy than to cut; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, if the corruption is in the wrist or ankle; si est mout fort celle chose, but this is a very strong measure; mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; nonetheless, you must investigate how it opens up to you; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, and cleanse it in every way possible; mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; but ensure that the vein or nerve does not hinder you; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, know that there are many knives and saws for cutting these bones; selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, according to the position of the bones and their appearance; et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, and their thickness and subtlety; et lor grandor et lor petitece, and their size and smallness; et lor duresce; and their hardness; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; therefore, you must prepare for each type of work its instrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, and know that the work will show you the instrument you need; selonc la conissance de cest art, according to the knowledge of this art; et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; and the testimony of the methods of illnesses; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient. consider the instrument you need according to what is required.
dou feu	 of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The head of the member rots from within or without; and when you have treated that rotting with the cure of medicines, and they do not benefit at all, it is necessary to cut off that member until the place where the rotting comes, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater evil, which is the defect of the member; and the sign is that the member turns black, as if it were burnt by fire, and rots after the blackness, then this corruption goes from member to member, and takes over the entire body; therefore, hasten to cut [it off], and if it is due to the bite of some venomous creatures, such as a sea scorpion or viper, etc., if the rotting is at the top of the foot, cut it, and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it comes to the hand, cut it at the joint, so that the corruption does not spread to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, cut it with a knife; and if it passes the knife, it is death, and no amputation helps except for the amount of its strength; and do the same when corruption comes to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, cut it after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, cut off the whole foot; and if it rises in the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy than to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or sawing the limb is such that you bind it above and below, and stretch one assistant the lower band down, and another assistant the upper band up, and you remove the flesh between the two bands to a width of one thumb, until the bone is exposed; then cut or saw, and place on each side a cloth of linen, so that the saw does not touch the healthy part, and another lesion and abscess come to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And if blood flows when you operate, cauterize the place immediately, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is completed, then bind the wounded limb with a suitable ligature, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you that there was a man in our country: he had a blackness that looked like a burn from fire, and this corruption first came into his foot, so much so that it spread to the whole foot; and when the man saw the corruption, he hastened to cover the foot, and was healed; and a long time after, the corruption returned to the finger of the hand, and he came to me, and I put on repressive things after cleansing the body, and could not stop the corrosion; and he wanted me to cut his hand, and I did not want to, because I hoped to repel the matter; and I also feared that if I cut his hand, he might die, for the man's strength was weak; and he became completely desperate, and returned to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; and I have not heard of this happening except in cases where others have need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Sometimes an abscess forms in a fleshy part of the body and lingers so long that it accumulates much pus; then it bursts and perforates, and out jumps the pus, and the place remains empty, like a vessel; and the skin above is as thin as finely woven cloth, but does not reach the bone or nerve. Such an illness is called "sinus," not "fistula"; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone in depth, then it is called "fistula"; and such skin can be cut all around, even when it is thin, like finely woven cloth; and does not tear due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if you believe that the skin is inflamed, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, cure it thus with a clyster: observe whether the breast is large, and the bowel that comes out of it has a foul odor, then clysterize with Egyptian medicine made as follows: take an equal amount of absinthe, oil, and lead, put them to cook in one vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take some according to your need, dissolve it in water and honey, and clysterize the breast, and constrict the orifice; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then extract it by pressing out; do this many times until the breast is cleansed, and the pus is removed. And sometimes you will clysterize with ashes water when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ash from a grapevine stem, and pour water on top of it, then strain it, and clysterize until you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot endure it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the ashes water, then clysterize with water and honey in which there is a little ground lead. Or you will clysterize with honey and wine mixed together, where the honey has the property of cleansing and washing, and the wine makes the flesh inflamed; and when you have done this, and you believe that the breast is well cleansed, then clysterize it with what produces flesh in it, and it is that you take diafinite plaster, dissolve it with rose oil and in wine. Or you will clysterize it with some medicines and onions, of which I have spoken about their properties in the treatise on onions; and if the orifice of the breast is small, and the tube of the clyster cannot enter, then widen it a little with an iron, and insert a tampon of Egyptian ointment, or basilic ointment until it is widened. And if the wound is too large, sew up some of it leaving only one place where the clyster can enter, and if the orifice that excretes bowels is on top, then cut lower where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 Car when the abscess is full, it does not allow flesh to enter; and if you cannot close the wound below as you wish, then prepare it in such a manner that the abscess runs to the lowest place there is, for when the abscess is full, it does not allow flesh to enter. And if you cannot close the wound below as you wish, then prepare it in this manner: let the abscess run lightly downward and leave nothing of the abscess; and take consolidative medicines to put on the wound, and extend over a linen cloth that covers all the wound; then close firmly at the edges of the wound the opening of the breast as wide as before, then extend soft ointment on another cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it on the opening of the wound to lighten the abscess, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days once; and that which is over the opening of the breast, remove often to remove the abscess, and know what runs out of the abscess, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has been extended in this manner and you see the nature that rises on the opening of the wound, know that the breast is already healed, and the health approaches; and then unbind it in the morning, or the third day, and when you unbind the wound, then change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	 And if the breast throws out undigested food after many days, know that the breast does not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poison comes after a long time, do not despair of health, for healing approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 And there are men in whose wounds tardy healing of flesh occurs, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested food comes from the breast after many days, know that the breast does not heal; and if the breast is delayed in healing, and is remote, then apply dry medicines moistened in substance but dry in virtue, such as ointment of diaphoretics, for there is a large part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take ointment of diaphoretics, and make it with rose oil, and anoint it with old wine equal in substance; then cook and use it; and the same cooked thickened better when the ointment of diaphoretics is not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and frankincense, and grind them, and powder them on honey when it is over the fire; and then glue a cloth, and place it on the breast, and sometimes add long mastic, and roots of celestial lily, which is also like flour of chickpeas and cumin; and use them in simple or compound form: grind them, and make powder, and put on the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and not cured by this cure, then know that corruption is deep, and makes an impression on the bone, or on hard members, or on the joints; then treat it as a treatment for fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	 of the fingertip
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 Panaris is an abscess that forms under the fingertip of the hand or foot, or it may form in other places; and when it is neglected, if one does not take care, then a foul-smelling abscess comes, and it runs and throws pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps it will run all the way to the bone; and decay occurs as far as the bone, causing a putrid pain, and the tip of the finger is swollen, and the color is reddish.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help at all, then you must cut off with a hot iron all the excess that remains of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is very helpful if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy; and if the nail presses into the flesh, and begins to prick and wound it, you must place a thread under the nail that pricks the flesh, and push it upwards, and cut away that flesh subtly and lightly, and apply medicines burning and corrosive on the remaining flesh to remove everything; then treat with ointments until healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corruption is in the bone, you cut it out and pull hard, for as long as the rotten bone remains there, it cannot heal; and if you see the toe begin to rot, you cut it off as before mentioned, then treat until healed; and if it is struck and swollen, and causes great pain, you must first cleanse it; then cut the nail with a sharp spatula by sawing across the top, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh under the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, apply something soothing.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	 The pain of the deafness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The two joints that sometimes appear in the hands of some men are all fleshy, and sometimes there is bone in them, and sometimes there is a nail, and sometimes they grow from the root of the joint, or the growth appears in some people's fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 That which appears in any node of the finger does not move, and that which appears at the joint of the finger, perhaps moves; the size of the fleshy one is light, in this way: cut it off at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	 That which appears at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; therefore, be cautious.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In him who is born with or must remove the last joint, it is necessary that you first cut the flesh roundly until the bone, then cut the bone with an appropriate saw, then cure it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	 The joining that occurs in the fingers together is due to birth, or from wound scarring, or from fire cautery, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 Then you must cut this joint so that the fingers may be rejoined according to their natural forms; then place between two linen cloths or rags moistened in rose oil, so that they do not join together; or place between two thin sheets of lead until the place is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	 If suddenly one of his fingers comes with the palm, strike that joint as needed.
des vils	 from the filth
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 The veins are large and swollen, full of harmful melancholic substances that affect many parts of the body; they occur more frequently in the legs of those who walk, work, and carry things than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	 Therefore, you should administer to him a purging of black bile, and then heal with basilicum.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The treatment of iron is according to two methods: one is that you strike them and draw out the black blood; and the other method is that you raise the vein and draw it out entirely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The bleeding is done in this manner: first, raise the leg with very hot water until the large vein becomes thin, then hold the patient's leg from above the hip to below the knee; then strike the vein in one place or two or three, making a wide cut, then raise it and draw out the black blood by hand from one end to the other, as much as the patient can tolerate; and then bandage it, and instruct him to eat foods that purge black bile; and repeat the evacuation and healing when the veins are full, and this benefits the patient. ‌
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The lifting of it is according to this manner: lift the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then place it in a bath, and wash the leg with hot water until it becomes red, and swell the veins; and if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then cut towards the vein from the knee to the ankle; then work the skin with tweezers, and peel the vein from each side, until it appears when touched; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it looks like a white thread; then push the root downwards, so that it is raised from the skin, and then pinch it lightly with tweezers, then cut in another place above three fingers; then peel the skin over the vein until it appears, then lift it with tweezers as you have done before, and pinch it in another tweezers as you did first; then make another cut, or several if you need them, then lift and cut at the toe of the foot, then draw and lift up to the second cut; then draw from cut to cut, until it comes out completely, then cut; and if you cannot draw and lift it, then insert a needle with all one strong thread double, and lift and draw it, and insert it below a root, and turn your hand from side to side, until it comes out; and be careful that it does not break, for if it breaks, it cannot be drawn or lifted, and it brings harm to the patient; and when you have drawn it all, place wool soaked in wine and rose oil on the place of the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the face is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not cut it off; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The form of the iron from which one cuts the face is curved, and does not cut, so that it does not cut the vein; and it is thickly curved, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and here is the form:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is located in the legs, in hot parts where no grass or tree grows, and in dry land; and it may happen elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens due to the decay that comes under the skin, as it happens inside the body with serpents and worms, injected between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the sign of the beginning of this vein is that a very great inflammation comes in the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to come out like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 And if the head opens, it is necessary that you wrap around a piece of lead from three and a half to two and a half [inches], and the knot, and let the lead hang on the leg, and every time some comes out with the pus, wrap it around the lead, and the knot; and if it is too long, cut part of it off, and wrap the rest, and do not cut it at its root until it is completely issued; for if you cut it, it enters into the flesh, and causes an abscess and putrefaction in the place, and a serious illness; therefore it is necessary that it be treated little by little until the end, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this vein, when it is treated from five palms long, or ten, and one man came to me whose it issued ten palms long, and when you cut it, it expels I rays or holes, and pierce to the bottom so that all comes out; and let the matter inside be emptied, and apply medicines that prevent putrefaction every day, then treat it as abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes at this vein there is less blood, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot, or on the foot, and then much pus comes out, and from which blood gushes forth; treat it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called in our land "cattle disease," because it often happens to cattle, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body ascending and descending, and one feels it well when moving from limb to limb, until it destroys the skin where it goes, and blood gushes forth; and it is engendered by the putrefaction of certain humors, just as come worms and snakes and leeches and ascarides in the belly; and one fears its harm, for when it goes through the body, and it ascends to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps it enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
