Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see him curing and drawing it out, one cannot do so unless he goes: therefore, you must tie the place above and below with a strong bond very tightly, then cut above and draw it out forcefully; and if the pus is deep in the flesh and you cannot find it, then cauterize it with fire on top until it dies. And one of the greatest harms it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming towards the head near the eye, then hold firmly under it the sorcil, then cut above, and draw it out forcefully; and the patient must use purging medicines to cleanse the body of bad humors and abstain from foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 From the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called in our land "vakirir," and it is a pain that comes to certain members, and then moves from one member to another; and I have seen what I tell you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	 I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and a short time later, I saw it rise like a worm to the shoulder, faster than anything else, just as if quicksilver runs from one place to another; the pain left that place, and fixed itself in the shoulder, and then a short time later it ran through the whole body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it always turns around the body, as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	 Je me merveillais beaucoup comment elle se déplaçait ainsi d'un membre à l'autre, car je n'avais jamais vu cette maladie sous cette forme auparavant.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	 Cependant, j'avais vu beaucoup de personnes qui avaient ressenti des douleurs passant d'un endroit à un autre, mais je ne l'avais jamais vu se produire comme je le vis chez la femme; et je me dis que cela était parce que les femmes ont un corps sec, et des veines découvertes, et pour cette raison apparaissent ces ventosités contraintes; et ce n'est pas le cas selon cette raison chez ceux qui sont délicats, et qui ont des corps humides et des veines remplies.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	 And when you see treating this illness, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, then tie it quickly above and below, and then cut into it until that swelling is forced out of place; and cauterize the area; and if you do not see it with your own eyes, then treat it with those who remove swellings, such as stinking pills, and serpent pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	 of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	 Arrows vary according to their appearances and the places on the body where they fall.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	 The diversity of arrows is such that there are those with large heads and small ones, barbed and unbarbed; and those with two prongs, and those with tongues, and those with pieces; and if an arrow falls into any limb, it does so in two ways: into a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, lungs, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	 When it falls into any part of these limbs, and the signs of death that I will tell you about later appear to you: then you must be careful with the extraction of this arrow, because many die in various ways; and when these bad signs do not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, draw it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	 And the signs of the head when the arrow falls into it and pierces the bone, are swelling and bruising on the forehead, as well as spots before the eyes, redness in the eyes, inflammation and redness of the tongue, seizures and confusion of the mind, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is discharge from the nose or ears; and perhaps he loses his speech and voice; and from the wound comes white, moist pus resembling brain matter, and also like a trickle of flesh; and if these signs appear to you, refrain from treatment, and draw out the arrow if it is not deeply embedded.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	 The signs of the arrow when it falls into the heart are that it is near the left nipple, and feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not hollow; and perhaps the arrow moves like a finger, and black blood comes out, and there is coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: then know without doubt that death follows.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	 And the sign of an arrow that has pierced the lung is that foam pours from the wound without pause, and the throat swells, and the patient changes color, and pants heavily and seeks cool air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	 And if the arrow falls into the covering of the ribs, it is near the small ribs; and there is great pain and great panting; and all the limbs move from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	 And if an arrow falls into the stomach, by chance some indigestible matter may jump out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	 And if an arrow falls into the belly, and some straw jumps out through the intestines, then there is no hope for a cure or for extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	 And if an arrow falls into the bladder, and the urine jumps out and comes forth, and the patient feels great pain, know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	 The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulders and arms and spine of the back and ribs and hips and legs and similar members, are safe according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	 Quant la saiette est en le nerf ou l’artere, et ele n’est venimouse, si conm te dirai ke me avint, por ceo que tu faces autretel.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	 It happened to a man that an arrow fell into his temple at the root of his nose; I tried it, and pulled it out from another side below the fat of the ear, and he was healed without harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	 And another time an arrow fell into the fat of the eye below the lid, and the arrow was turned back, and I could not reach anything but the point towards the shaft, and the arrow was large like a Turkish bow, all the iron light without ears; the youth was healed, and no evil happened to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	 And he drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabian with feathers: I shaved the beard, and refined until I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	 And he drew an arrow from a man who had fallen into the belly, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days had passed, his condition did not change; I cut above the arrow, and I drew it out strongly, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	 And I saw a man into whose back an arrow had fallen, and the wound was closed upon it; and the arrow remained inside him, and he did not change his natural disposition at all, nor did he find any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	 Et je vis un autre homme, chez qui une flèche tomba sur le visage, et la blessure fut soudée ; et il resta ainsi sans ressentir une grande douleur ; et beaucoup d'autres cas similaires.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	 And I drew an arrow from a man of the king's princes, which had fallen into his nose, and was slightly inclined to the right side; and the arrow was completely lodged there. I was called to treat it after it had fallen for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	 And I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	 I probed it with a very fine probe and did not feel anything; and he felt a pricking pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	 I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I placed on the spot an astringent and digestive poultice, so that the place would not swell; and the place of the arrow appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	 Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors,
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	 Je placed on the wound a corrosive medicine for several days, until it was open, and I probed it, and felt the tip of the arrow which was lodged there; then I approached the opening of the wound with that same corrosive medicine, until the tip of the arrow appeared visibly; and it lasted well for about four months, and then the wound healed so much that I inserted the pincers, and I pulled from one side and the other, and it could not come out; then I did not cease to be subtle and ingenious in using tools, until on one day I took hold of it with well-made pincers, according to how its form will be described at the end of this chapter, until I pulled it out, and closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	 And the doctor judges that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the patient was entirely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	 Or I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you may apply your care to those things which I do not say, for the book cannot include everything; but the wise master learns well from a small thing, and from those present and failing, he finds new work and new instruments for the application of strange things that happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	 I say that arrows should not be removed from the members into which they are struck except in two ways: either by the place where they enter or from another side; and those that come out by the place where they enter are called arrowheads entering fleshy places, and such happens sometimes now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	 And if it does not jump out now, let it stay until the flesh around it is rotten and the opening is cleared; and likewise if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, let it stay thus for a few days and move it each day; then it will jump out, and if it does not, pierce all around with a very fine needle until the place around is enlarged, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	 And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head and reaches one of the cavities of the brain, or any of the accidents I have mentioned happen to the patient: do not extract it, but let it stay until it becomes even after some days, for if the arrow comes to this place, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	 And if the arrow is not lodged firmly in the bone alone, and does not reach to the marrow, and the patient remains for some days without bad effects, then use the device for drawing it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it is firmly lodged in this manner and cannot be removed, then apply compresses around it, as I have told you; then treat the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	 And if the arrow is hidden in the body so that it cannot be seen, then search all over the wound; and if you feel it, then draw it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the narrowness of the wound, and the depth of the arrow, and there are no bones or nerves or veins, then enlarge the wound until it is large enough; and draw out the arrow if you can, and if there are barbs on the arrow that hold it in place, remove as much flesh from both sides as you can, and then bend or break the barbs of the arrow so that you can draw it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, lest you cause greater injury.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	 And if you cannot do it at once, leave it until the place around is rotten, then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	 And if the flow of blood is contrary to you, then manage it as we have said in the chapter on treatment; and beware of cutting the nerve or vein, and devise a way how you can safely extract the arrow, soon or late, strongly or gently; and place the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow fell into him, for this is the greatest help that there is, and if you cannot do this, then place him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	 The arrow that comes out from the other side, or something of it appears, or the skin is swollen in such a way that it can be seen or felt clearly: cut down on it, until the pincers can grasp it, and then pull it out: thus it will come out now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	 And if it is lodged in the bone, turn your hand smoothly until it enters the bone and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	 And if it cannot come out, leave it there and then begin the extraction again until it comes out strongly; and if part of the arrow remains, push in all of the shaft; and if the shaft is broken off, and you wish to administer pushing, administer an instrument with a notch into which the tip of the arrow enters; and then push hard, and if the arrow is splintered, insert an instrument with a pointed end to ease extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	 And if the arrow is poisoned, you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as necessary.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And if the arrow falls in the buttock or in the belly or in the bladder or in the side, and it is close to, and you can cut over it, if you cut; and beware of cutting the vein and the nerve, and then extract it, and then sew up the wound, if necessary; and treat until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	 The shape of the tongs used to remove arrows is like a bird's beak, and see here its shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	 And there are many types of them: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	 The shape of the pointy end is like the feather of a bird, to insert at the tip of the arrow, as in this form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	 The shape of the pincers for pushing and pulling is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	 the veins common to the body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	 There are XXXI veins that one can bleed from, of which there are XVI in the head, namely: two that are behind the ears, called "herbech"; and two arteries that appear on both temples; and two veins that are on the eyelids of both eyes, called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the two jugulars that are in the neck; and the two veins that are in the lips above the mouth, which are the veins called "augeherich"; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	 The veins that are commonly healed are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is located on the left side, and the common people call it "the vein of the head"; and the median is called "fast", and it is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and the common people call it "the vein of the heart"; and the basilic is also located on the right side, and the common people call it "the vein of the belly", and it is above the brachial, and this is the one that is healed, which clearly appears on the wrist.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	 And the salvatelle is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot there are three veins: one is below the bend of the wrist on the left side, and the second saphenous which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein which is called "nesse", which is at the ankle on the other side; and in the other leg there are also three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	 The bleeding of wounds that are after the ears helps with old catarrhs and migraines; and the qualities of the bleeder, as I tell you, is to raise the head of the patient and rub the place where the wounds are with a rough cloth; then let the patient pull his neck with a screw until two wounds appear behind the ears in two hanging places from the head: press them then with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, draw out blood; then take the lancet and push it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand over the whole vein, and cut well the skin and the vein two fingers' width across, and let the blood flow until you wish; then hold and bind until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	 The bleeding of the two veins that are in the two temples, it is good for an old migraine, and cold, and customary headache, and for the body of tearful eyes; and the qualities of the bleeder are as I say: and it is that the patient stretches his neck, until the two veins appear clearly; and he feels the pulse under your finger, then sign with ink; then lift the heart over the top vein to your finger's tip, and push the lancet underneath, and lift the vein high, and cut it, as you have done in two other veins, and let the blood flow according to your need; then release the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on; and then bind it well, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their covering and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	 Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	 And place the point on the vein, and strike with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the amount you wish; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed and sometimes use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	 However, it is not appropriate for the flame to be too sharp; and bleed obliquely, because the bone is nearby, and perhaps the sharp flame breaks when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	 The bleeding of the two veins that are in the two temples helps the eyes, and the skin, and the redness, and the eye-corner in the eye, and for diseases of the face; and the nature of their bleeding is such that the patient should twist his neck with some ligature, as before; then he bleeds, and let the blood flow be straight, a little long from the flame, somewhat wide, because there is no flesh there.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	 And if the flame is subtle, it may break; then make the blood flow as much as you need, and then tie off with a thread, and tie well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	 The bleeding of the vein of the nose helps against fever and epilepsy and diseases of the face such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, especially when it is old; and the nature of the bleeding is such that the patient should twist his neck, then hold his nose with your left hand, take a subtle, long flame, and insert it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow; and do not go too deep, and make the blood flow according to your needs, then tie off for one night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	 Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;
de la sainie des leivres	 of the bleeding of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	 The bleeding of the veins of the lips above helps to gather in the mouth, and the rotting of the gums, and the splitting of the lips, and of the nose and around it.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	 And the quality of the bleeding is to make the patient sit before you and tighten his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one of which is on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are recognized by being black, and by the fact that there are small black veins around them: therefore cut both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, cut the largest of each side, and do the same with the two veins that are above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 Of the bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The bleeding of the veins that are under the tongue helps after the bleeding of the cephalic, and this is for constricting the throat, and for diseases of the eye, and for diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the bleeder is such that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and he lifts his tongue, and looks under on each side a black vein: then bleed one and the other, and do not go too deep, because below are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins of the needle with which one usually bleeds are bled in two ways: either by pricking with an entirely wide and fat flame, or a subtle olive-shaped one like cutting needles, and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and subtle according to the width and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	 The shape of the flame is very renowned, and it is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	 And it is necessary to open the full veins that are filled with abundant visible blood and contain thick and cloudy blood; this is the shape of the olive flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	 And it is more subtle, pointed, and is for healing the subtle veins where there is subtle golden blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	 The healing of the basilica vein, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are under the throat and in the neck, chest, stomach; and it is necessary for the healer to heal wisely and to beware of the artery that is below.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	 And if he cuts the artery and blood begins to flow out, it is necessary to stop it, as I have said; and the flame should not be piercing, but rather cutting like a scalpel.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the basilica does not open clearly, then you must extract it and replace it with another; or seek any vein from it, or close the vein in its place within the arm: it opens clearly; and cut off the head with the flame quickly, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	 And if you wish to locate the bleeding site, first extract the blood from the arm until you feel the pulse; then mark the spot with ink, and then bind the arm, and cut off the vein with the flame quickly; and be careful not to strike an artery when you see the spot swell, for it is an artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you see it rise upward like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is from an artery: hurry then, and place your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood clots, which often happens; if it flows, let it be, and the patient must not move; and he must stay still until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	 And if the blood is not clotted and it flows away, and the physician is not present, cut the artery open, for the head of it draws back; and clot the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	 And take a piece of fig bark, and cut it in half, and take one half and tie it on well until the next day; if the blood clots, that is good; if not, then cure it as we have said, with powders that clot blood; and the clotting is not serious for many reasons due to the smallness of the wound, and the strength of the ligature of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The bleeding from the vein in the middle helps so that it draws blood from above and below, because it is composed of the basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is necessary for the person drawing the blood to be cautious for the nerve that is underneath, and if he presses too hard and finds the nerve, and it swells, and the wound becomes infected, then perhaps it cannot heal; and this nerve often appears, and if it does not appear in some men due to its subtlety, then you must draw blood with an instrument called "anesil"; and avoid the nerve as much as possible.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	 And if there is a vein between the two nerves, then make the incision lengthwise.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	 The bloodletting of the head aids in drawing blood from the head and helps the eyes; and one must bleed at the olive groove or the myrtle groove, because it is the safest of all veins, for there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	 However, one must seek the lightest place, and it is not harmful if one fails the first time and starts again; and perhaps the place swells in some men when one fails the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	 The quality of the bloodletting is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	 The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that bloodletting is only practiced to maintain health and to avoid future illnesses; and the bloodletting should be done in one of the three veins which are: cephalic, fast and basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of spring for the young, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of fullness appear; and one should bleed on the first or third day, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	 Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee,
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	 Ne the old who have passed sixty years should not be treated.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	 Ne one who wishes to be treated in any manner should first cleanse the intestines with a light enema, if he has retained much feces, so that the veins do not attract harmful superfluities from the intestines to the main members; nor should one be treated who is too filled with food, or who is drunk, as long as he is intoxicated, or dropsical; and one should refrain from treating after colic, vomiting, diarrhea, frequent intercourse with a woman, labor, staying awake, and fasting, and everything that reduces all the strength, whether by weapon wound or body injury. Then refine the humors if the blood is thick, through food and drink and medicines, if you have the power to do so; then enter the bath, if nothing prevents you, to refine the blood, and treat the vein of the foot around the third hour, as we have said; and guard yourself that day from work, from pain, and from lust and similar things. And be happy and joyful, and let the healer stand higher than the one being treated, and rub his arm two or three times, then draw out the vein moderately, for if it is drawn too tightly or loosely, the blood cannot flow; and then rub the spot with his hands until the veins swell and can be felt; then moisten the healer's finger with a little old oil, then place his index finger of his left hand on that vein under the spot where he wishes to treat, so that the vein does not burn and burst when pierced.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	 Car il y a des veines qui fuient comme des cordes au sainier, et il y en a d'autres qui sont pleines de ventosité, donc quand on met le feu dessus, la flamme recule et ne peut pas ouvrir la veine, et ainsi en est-il avec celles-ci; et si l'on perce la veine, alors la plaie est trop étroite, par conséquent il faut que le saigneur soit avisé de ces choses.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	 Et si la veine ne s'ouvre pas la première fois, c'est bien; sinon, recommence encore un peu en dessous de cet endroit ou immédiatement au-dessus, si l'endroit n'est pas gonflé.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	 And if the place is swollen, and the patient is frightened, let him wait for one or two days, and do not bind the arm: by chance such abscesses may form; do not enter into a bath, then restart the bleeding if he wishes; and if the opening is small, and the blood runs subtly, and you doubt that it will come out as much as you see, then fire into that same opening all the flame directly; and hasten the work quickly, before the place becomes swollen; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	 If you see the place swollen, do not restart the bleeding, and put a little oil on it, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the oil is better than oil; and thus administer the oil of oil in each bleeding that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and this same action and boil of them, when one puts it on the place; then the blood becomes subtle and separates when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	 And if there comes a large abscess, which happens often, especially when it is not cauterized before that time or the opening of the vein is small, then hasten and place on the area a wet sponge in water and a little hot wine, and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the issue of blood from the vein. And if there remains on the area after some days any darkness or greenness, it does not harm him; and if you see, place on the area something of aloes or myrrh mixed in calamint juice, mustard, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	 And often an abscess and appearance occur at the cautery of the vein: then place your hand on it, and if you find the area soft under the pressure of the hand, that appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Eschui therefore that you do not put on any of the things we have mentioned, for perhaps it comes out without the artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the place, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	 And draw from each according to the quantity of its power and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	 For if the blood is black, let it out until it is red; and if you see it thick, let it out until it is refined; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	 And it is necessary that for the one who is strong and vigorous, and needs to have blood let out, that a larger wound be made, and that the flame should be wide; and for the weak one, do the opposite, and he must be bled often and frequently, and one should bleed him by cutting across, not by pricking; and this method of bleeding is safe from excessive bleeding and nerve injury, and is worth more than long or wide bleeding.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	 And to the person whose body is lacking at the wound, one should give moist bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is hot, then draw blood three or four times. And if he is of cold complexion, let him chew before the bleeding moist bread in must syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, chickpeas, and well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	 And if he faints at the wound after much blood loss, then let him smell a broth of meat and subtly scented syrup, and use the other things that we have said in the section or chapter on syncope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	 And if he wants to slash his arm, and bleed another time, then it is necessary, when he is weakened by great bleeding, that he bleeds a little at a time, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	 And whoever wants to slash his arm after the first bleeding, and he has a strong body, then let him bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	 And whoever wants to bleed from another place, then he should bleed on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	 Because there is much blood in the body which is already heated and causes fever; therefore it is necessary to draw out a large quantity, and widen the orifice until it flows abundantly; then you should observe all the conditions of bleeding, and place your hand on the pulse when he bleeds, so that death does not come in place of blood; and this happens many times when the bleeder is negligent; and it is not necessary when you see the arm released, and blood comes out a second time, and the orifice is closed, that you press very hard; nor if it is crooked, should he extend the arm hastily, for that would be bad; but leave it until it bleeds a second time; or you may puncture at the tip of the flame, so that the blood which is frozen at the mouth of the vein comes out with force, and place on I pound of linen cloth in water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	 Et s'il y a une enflure dans la veine, alors laissez-la sans la presser, jusqu'à ce que l'abcès soit calmé.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	 And if it is necessary to draw blood a second time, then heal it in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	 The veins in the arm are healed in the place of the head's vein because it is composed there.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	 And the manner of healing is such that the patient puts his hand in hot water until the flesh is red; then it should be tied moderately so that the vein appears well, and then heal transversely, not widely or lengthwise; and let the opening be wide, and heal near the joint of the hand. And if blood does not come out, put the hand back in hot water, and let the blood run into the water until you have enough. And in summer, do not put the hand back in hot water, for one puts it more in winter than in summer; and the healing from this vein is safer than from all other veins, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	 The bleeding of the vein at the back of the right hand is effective for all liver diseases, and this is how it is done: hold the hand tightly and pour in hot water until the vein swells, if you see it; and if the blood flows crookedly, and you cut all around, it will not harm anything; and do not go too deep, because the nerves are bare beneath all the skin, and then put the hand back in hot water, if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	 And when you have drawn as much blood as needed, then place oil and wax on the vein to seal it quickly, and do this for each time.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	 The flow of blood from his left hand is equal to the disease of the mouse, and acts just as I have told you towards the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	 The flow of blood from the spleen is equal to all the diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the womb, and retention of the menses, and disease of the kidneys, and of the thighs and ancient legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	 And the quality of its bleeding is that the patient should put his foot in hot water, and rub over the vein until it bursts, and bind above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot there are many veins; then bleed it at the largest vein or at the ankle, which is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	 Et si tu le traites sur le pied, fais attention aux nerfs qui se trouvent en dessous, et traite la plaie en travers comme en coupant; et que la flamme soit stable.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	 And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water and let the wound drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	 And if the bleeder fails the first time, then start again a second time above a little, because the place is salty; do not worry about the nerve as we have said, and do the same for the top of the other foot.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	 The place of the sciatic vein is at the back of the ankle, and its bleeding helps with hip pain when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	 And the quality of its bleeding is such that the patient enters the bath and twists four times around the ankle, because otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then bleed in all ways you can, and by crossing; and it is worth noting that you should cup it, because the place is hollow, and it is very responsive to many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	 And if you cannot find it, then bleed some vein that opens at the back of the foot, towards the little toe, and beware of the nerves; and let as much blood flow out as you wish, and then untie the knot, and place cotton and bind it; she is now bled.
des sainies de ventouse	 of cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	 Ventouses are made from horns, or brass, or glass; and venesection is done in two ways: either by bleeding and drawing blood, or without bleeding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	 And this venesection which is without bleeding is done in two ways: either with fire or without fire; and venesection which is done by bleeding and blood extraction is performed in fourteen places on the body, one of which is entirely at the top of the head; and another is in the neck; and two others on both sides of the neck; and the cupping glass below the chin; and the cupping glass on both shoulders; and the cupping glass on the buttocks; and the cupping glasses on both arms; and the cupping glasses on both legs; and the cupping glasses on both ankles; and venesection does not draw blood, except from small veins scattered throughout the flesh, and therefore it weakens no one at all, just as one does by bleeding a vein; and it is not necessary that it be administered, either with fire or without fire, in any illness that comes from repletion, until the entire body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	 And if by necessity of illness one must be cupped, or for custom, then we administer it every hour at the beginning of the month, and in the middle, and at all times; because there are such people who, when they need to be cupped, have a heavy head; and there are those who find fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and in the neck, and darkness in the eyes; and there are those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and spit blood; and there are those who dream, and see nothing but blood and wounded and dead things and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	 And when we see these signs, especially when it is in the middle of the month, we order cupping after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	 The bleeding of the nose is helpful for the headache … that comes to the eyes, and it should not be done after the evacuation of the entire body; and this ventilation is in place of the cephalic bloodletting, and it should not be used by those of cold complexion or who have catarrh, because this does them great harm; and therefore it is not suitable for the elderly to use it, nor for those who have cold diseases of the head.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	 And those who bleed often, become stupid, and therefore it is necessary to place the cupping glass a little lower due to the fear of becoming stupid.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	 The cupping in the neck is in place of the bloodletting of the head and the basilica, and therefore it is useful for constriction of the foot, and for cleft palate, and for jaundice, and for dropsy; and there it should be applied gently, because if it is held too firmly, it injures the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	 The ventosations at the two ribs of the neck are good for headaches, migraines, and strangulation, and for toothache, and are in place of the venesection of the basilica; and you must instruct the practitioner to express with his hand when inserting, so that he does not cut the artery, and prevent the flow of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	 The ventosations under the chin are good for diseases of the mouth and for the decay of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and they take the place of the venesections of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	 The ventosations of the shoulders are good for diseases that come from heat and inflammation.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	 The punctures of the ribs are as valuable as those of three veins in the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; and instruct the surgeon not to strike too deeply, for the place is bare of flesh, and beneath lie nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	 The cupping on the buttocks is as valuable for hemorrhoids of the anus, and for diseases below, and it must be large, and of copper, that it may draw well; and by chance, if it were too fine, it would break; and this makes great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	 The cupping of the legs heals openly, for they draw blood from the whole body, and are valuable against old pains of the kidneys, and of the spleen, and of the bladder, and remove fevers; and they are in the place of the two sophenes, and the two ankles, but nevertheless they weaken the body after long use, and cause fever in many constitutions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	 The manner of applying the cupping glass is such that you first apply it empty, and suck immediately, and place it quickly, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing this until you see the place red and swollen, and apparent are the veins of blood; then strike, and reapply the cupping glasses, and take care in the arrangement of the body, for there are such that have dark flesh, and clear pores: thus it is necessary to strike only once, and it is necessary to make large wounds, and a few deep ones; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	 And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to thin the course of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	 And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw out the blood little by little, we are satisfied with just one strike.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we wish to draw much blood, then bleed often; and if the blood is thick, strike deeply into the vein, so that the heart may be suddenly pierced, and those who have thick and hard skin, and whose pores are narrow, must apply oil to the places where the cups will be placed: in summer, use violet oil, or oil of sweet almonds, or oil of cucurbit seeds; and in winter, use cresson oil, or lily oil, or camomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	 And if the excess is large and cold, take bitter oil, or balm oil, or dill oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 And if the one being treated has tender flesh and large pores, no oil should be put on it, but it should be washed after ventosation with rose water, or cold water, or mallow water, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or another similar [liquid].
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	 And if he has much moisture, raise it with oil of citrus, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 And those who have large superfluities raise them with old wine, or juice of the cabbage, or decoction of dill or chamomile, or other similar [things]; and they should not be treated with cupping before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and one must not sleep after cupping, and one should wash themselves before cupping and when they have been cupped.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And guard against those who are healing if they are choleric, and if their blood is too hot and inflamed; then it is necessary that they take cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuce in vinegar, and similar things; and eat less, and meat from a castrated animal, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And those who have a cold complexion should take syrup of honey, and moderately scented wine, which is between old and new, and eat little, and eat less meat and small birds and thrushes; and on the day he will be ventosed, he must drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men sometimes a triple or musk before or after ventosing, to strengthen the main limbs; and let the blood be refined, but it is not necessary for those who are hot to drink it.
