Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the break is near the shoulder, then you must place I tendon in the middle below the axillary, and the other towards the elbow, below the break; and so if the break is towards the elbow, then you should place I tendon lightly, without effort, until the break is level on the place and on the elbow; then set the break equal, as it should be, and tighten it, in case swelling does not occur.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	 And if an abscess comes there, do not strain it until the seventh day, and place a wet cloth on linen and rose oil, so that this abscess be calmed; then strain it, and the manner of straining is such that you place the plaster on the break, then assemble the arm onto the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; and put the bandage, and strain on the shoulder and on the arm, so that the arm be in its proper place, if anything prevents it, or if the bone is not displaced.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	 And if you doubt that the bone may move, use splints, and place on the fracture a splint wider and stronger than the others, with two finger-widths between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes the fracture three fingers on either side; then strain on the splints, as I have said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less widely spaced.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 Et si tu vois l'assise des esteles, et l'estrignement, ainsi que nous avons dit, à l'heure où tu restaures le membre brisé, et tu doutes de la chaleur de l'apostème, alors laisse-le lier jusqu'au septième jour, comme nous avons dit; puis regarde chaque trois jours le lien, afin que démangeaison ou gonflement n'y viennent pas au lieu, où le soin ne puisse venir au membre pour cela qu'il est trop serré.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 Et s'il l’accepte, ainsi que nous avons dit.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 Et si aucun tel accident n'y survient pas, alors ne le délie pas avant trois jours ou plus, et que le patient dorme sur son dos, et ait ses mains sur son ventre; et mette sous l'épaule un coussin plein de laine également, et regarde chaque heure du jour ou de la nuit, que la forme du membre brisé ne change pas, ou que le lien ne soit pas relâché; s'il l’accepte par la vertu de la médecine, et lui donne la nourriture que nous avons mentionnée plus tôt, de manière que la nourriture soit d'abord subtile; et quand il commence à récupérer, qu'elle soit plus épaisse.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset within forty days in total; and then one should unbind and administer a bath and ointments for the place to heal.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the stricture is foul and plugged, it stays bound for one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	 of the break in the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	 The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the two "radius"; one is small, and it follows the wrist; and the other is large, and it is beneath, towards the little finger; perhaps only the large radius breaks, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small radius is broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when the large one is broken, then the healing is bad, and more grievous than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is the small fibula that is broken alone, then you should lightly extend it slightly and set it straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large fibula, then you must stretch it more strongly; and extend it on a cushion, and take the little finger of the hand higher than the others, and the small toe lower than the other toes, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then the minister should extend his arm to the part below his hand, or at the ankle, and another minister on the other side above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 Then let the physician set it straight, according to its best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if in the break there are pieces, then place each one in its proper place; and if any of them is protruding that pricks the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut above it and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	 And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken about it in a specific chapter; so take the treatment from there.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And if in the beginning of the treatment abscesses occur, then apply a cloth of plaster made from rose oil and white wax, which should not be too hard nor too soft; and tie the cloth delicately on top until those abscesses are relieved.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 And then remove the plaster, and apply the emplastrum of flour with plenty of egg, then place the splints, and let the splint on the fracture be a little stronger and a bit wider than the others; and know that there should be six splints for the arm in several positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and hold it tighter over the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as they are being placed, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths on the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread with which it is tied be linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And restore the member and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if any bad accident happens to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then you must rinse the member with hot water until this itching is appeased; and let the member rest not too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then begin the binding again, and if the ligament is softened and the bone separated, or similar things, then set it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	 And beware if the nourishment cannot reach the member because it is too tight; then you must soften it in a pouch and leave it thus for some days until the nourishment reaches there, and then bind it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 And if none of these things that we have said happen to the patient, then do not unbind until twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 Or if around the neck, then let him put his hands to his neck, and let his neck be even, and he should watch for movement and turning, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture is restored in thirty or thirty-five days, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the combinations and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	 of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	 Know that at the back of the hand and in the vicinity of the fingers there are few breaks, and nothing but sprains often happen there.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	 And when the palm of the hand is broken or sprained, it is necessary that the patient sit on his knees and sit upright in front of him evenly; then put his hand on a stretched cloth, and let the assistant stretch the broken bones, and let the physician set them straight until they are well joined; and apply the bandage and the compresses, if there is no abscess, then apply a splint according to the size of the place; and let it be wrapped in one layer of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	 And if the break is around the pelvic area near the stomach of the foot, make a sphere from rags, and instruct the patient to press it against their broken foot; then bind it with a long rag, and let the end be as soft as the palm of the hand, and bind it as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	 And if the break is in the finger, you must place a bandage on top and another beneath the finger, so that the hand remains open and straight; then bind it all around the hand, and secure the tie between the two fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	 And if the break occurs in one of the toes, whether it is protruding, make it even as needed; and bind it with the foot, and if you see fit, place a small straight bandage to raise the break, so that it does not move; and if the break is in other toes, such as in the big toe or one of the others, make it even, and tie it with the healthy toe that follows; or bind them all together, whichever works better, or place a bandage on top, as for the big toe; and be careful in the restoration and arrangement of an abscess, and support those who come to assist, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	 of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	 The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it can be seen clearly when it turns forward and backward; and the restoration is such that one end is tied above the break, and the other below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	 And the patient lies on his back, then each assistant extends his ligature evenly to his side; and this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then one of the ligatures should be towards the knee, and the other ligature below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And likewise if it is near the knee, then let the ligature be near the knee, and the extension below; then let the physician place the bone evenly in his two hands, so that it may be according to its natural shape, and then apply the poultice, and bind it, unless pus comes out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	 And if there is a hot abscess, let it calm down before returning to your work and treatment; the procedure is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 It is necessary that you wrap around the break two or three layers of strong bandages, leaving an excess of material, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the base of the toe, and pass a long thread between the thigh and the leg, near the knee below, and the ends of the thread come up; then turn around the leg and the thigh the bandage, then place splints on the break, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloth to make the pressure even, then begin to tie firmly three or four turns on the break; and as you go higher on the break, tighten it less; then take hold of the two ends of the thread that you have passed between the leg and the thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then return below to the end of the thread, until you reach near the foot; and make sure it does not move from its place, then leave it so, if there is no abscess or swelling or any other similar thing.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And if it happens, dislocate it, and address the issue as we have said many times; and if there are bone fragments that protrude, they should be removed if possible; and if not possible, then split the area, and pull hard; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	 Sometimes the hip is broken in such a way that pins are inserted, as in the shoulder and arm; however, the patient does not limp with this type of restoration.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	 And know that the hip is restored in seven days, or a little less or more, depending on the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	 from the calf of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the kneecap, a fracture occurs rarely, but it bends frequently.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 And if it breaks, it is only a crack or a hole, and this happens to all wounds, and without wounds, and everyone feels this well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the restoration is like this: put what is round equally on both sides until it can be assembled together; then apply the plaster, and put a round bandage on it if needed, and bind it as necessary, then follow all the arrangements that we have said for other fractures, such as abscesses and others; and for each accident, give what is needed until it heals. 
de la brisure de la jambe	 Of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 You should know that in the leg there are two bones: one of which is rightly called «mustelz», and the other is called «foscile». And all fractures that occur in it come to the arm as well, and for this reason, the restoration is just like that of the arm, and the workings are entirely the same. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns on all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	 And if the thin bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 And if the thick bone is broken, one feels great pain and sees it well; and it turns downward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then apply traction, and align it evenly, and bind the splints evenly; but nonetheless, if the fracture is ugly and there are many fragments, then the traction should be less and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you have completed your work, take two splints of wood that fit the leg on each side, and let them be as long as the leg from the knee downwards; then wrap around them in two places one bandage above and one below, and tie it in the middle as well, and at this time the leg cannot bend to the right or to the left, and thus it is good; and some place on it one or more bands along the length of the leg, and it is of wood, and they put the leg in it to prevent movement, and this is properly done when there is a fracture with a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess hot or other accident; then cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	 Of the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	 At the ankle there is no break, but sometimes in the bones of the foot and in two places, and it happens more often that they are fractured in several ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	 And if there is a break in the bones of the foot, and you see that these bones overlap each other, then place the sick person’s foot on the ground as if he wanted to walk, and now put your foot on his, where the bones are raised, then press until they return to their places; then apply the poultice and stuffing on top, and under the bottom of the foot place a small board with two flat legs, then bind it tightly around the foot, and after you have wrapped bandages around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	 And when three days or four have passed, release the ligament, for you will find the bones equal, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	 And if any of the two bones are broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint on the broken finger according to its length and somewhat wider, then place under the foot the board I mentioned, and bind it tightly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken bones, place a splint on each bone according to its size, wrapped in a linen cloth, and bind the board under the foot; and let it be standing on top of the board above the belly of the foot, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	 And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, just as we have said; and treat each incident as it should be treated.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	 of the break in the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the woman's natural bone is broken, make her sit widened, then incline her towards the back part, and let her be held from behind; then fill the woman's natural cavity with cotton, and put in as much as I have said; then make the woman stand up, and lift the back little by little, and then the cotton jumps out until it comes to the entrance of the natural cavity, and the bone returns with the stone; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and do this for seven days or thereabouts: then the fracture will be restored, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and tie a reed to the opening, and blow up the entire bladder in the natural cavity; then blow strongly into the reed until the bladder is inflated inside: the natural cavity will also heal the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like this for some days until it heals.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 And when the bones of the wrist of a man are broken, or of a woman, restore them as we have said for the hip bone; and these fractures are not hidden from those who apply their study and practice, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 Because a fracture signifies many different ways of restoration; therefore consider this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	 In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose quill and insert the penis into it; then wrap cloth around it, and leave it for three days or until it heals, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	 of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	 It is necessary for someone who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as the hip bone or shoulder, that they be healed immediately, as the bandages we have mentioned demonstrate.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the wound heals, restrain it with vitriol, if you have nothing else, then begin again to restore the break in that same hour, or on that day, if pus does not form there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	 And if pus forms there, leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the pus is subdued, and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you would cause a bad outcome.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	 And if the broken bone is protruding above the skin, then you must gently grasp it between your fingers with slight tension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	 And if the tension is not equal in your hands, then reset it with this iron instrument which has seven or eight teeth and is as wide as the wound requires; and therefore it is necessary for the physician to have three or four of these, according to what he needs for each fracture treatment; and let it be round and a little thick so that it does not bend at the compression on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp at the front and thicker towards the middle, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "palainche," for which the curved head should be placed on top of the visible bone; and push once until it returns, and let them be equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot well take hold of the bone, then you must cut off the head of the bone, so that the instrument may have power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	 And if you cannot bring back the bone as we have said, then cut with an appropriate instrument for this purpose, either a knife or saw, to your ability; then remove that which remains in the bone by roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 So that it is in its place, then moisten the cloth in black stiptic wine, and properly so if it is on the stomach; and do not put any ointment or other oil-based substance on the wound, lest it cause putrefaction and corruption; then administer splints after you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the covering all around according to the size of the wound, and take great care that the wound is not constricted with the fracture; and many times foolhardy physicians have done this, causing death or corruption in the patient; and let the binding be softer and gentler than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that evil may happen to it, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then you should not apply bandages; but wrap around, instead of bandages, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one or two days that the swelling increases at the wound, then remove everything you have placed on it, and apply a healing ointment to the wound, such as a tetrapharmacum ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	 And you must unbind the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	 And the limb should be prepared in such a way that the swelling runs down gently.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	 And if many days pass, and it cannot heal but returns always swollen, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must probe the wound with a tent, and remove all these loose pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if a fistula comes to the place, or another form of corruption, then you must cure it, according to what is said in this previous chapter.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and opens on the limb, such as the thigh bone or shoulder blade, and other similar large limbs, do not pull it out, for many times death results, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall out by itself after twenty days or thirty, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	 The blows that come upon the suture
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	 We often see this after the healing of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it is a terrible thing to see the limb's shape; and perhaps the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Take care then if the wound is fresh: and administer astringent medicines such as aloes, frankincense, myrrh, gum arabic, acacia, and similar others, so that you take some of these things or all together and mix them with astringent wine or plenty of egg or with vinegar; and put them on the knot in bandages, and bind it well, and do not unbind it for many days; and then unbind it, and start another one, until the nodules are removed; or you can apply it to a well-made piece of lead; for the property of lead is such that it removes all swellings on the limbs; and if the nodule has already turned into hardness like stone, and it needs to be removed, cut above it, and reveal the apparent superfluity; or give it to a rasher, until it is removed, and treat it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	 of the limb which is weak after recovery
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	 When the bone fracture is healed, but the limb remains weak and fragile afterwards, this happens for many reasons: one of which is because it was bound too tightly, and not bound as it should have been; or because there were too many bindings, and nourishment could not reach the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or due to excessive movement, not at the appropriate time; or because there is little blood in the body, making it weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	 And the cure is such that you make the patient eat, and make the body soft, until the blood is increased within it; and administer baths, and give joy and happiness; then apply pitch to the limb, so that the pitch draws abundant nourishment to it, and frequently wash it with warm water, until the nourishment reaches the limb; and it returns to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	 of a twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	 When the limb is twisted after healing, and the broken bones are open, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say that one should break the limb anew, and many foolish doctors have done this in our land; and these works are blamed, and great evils come from them, and perhaps death. However, if the swellings and tortures are recent, then they must be softened with hot water, or softening herbs should be cooked, such as leaves of marsh mallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and make a softening poultice, well made, and take the marsh mallow paste, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and apply the poultice on top. Or take fat figs, and grind them with colon spikenard powder, and similar medicines that reduce swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes dislocation is removed by rubbing continually and at length with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And let there be gentle movements of the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	 And if the deformity has become swollen and hardened, like stone, and must be removed with a knife, it should be cut to the bone, with a delicate incision gently; and put effort and skill into the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	 Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	 Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	 When dislocation comes to someone, it must be immediately returned without delaying.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 Car if one delays, the place swells, and perhaps it is only with difficulty that one can reset it to its place; therefore, it is not necessary to move it when it is swollen: many times it brings on shock and other pains; however, when this happens, make the patient drink a sanative potion, then leave them until the abscess subsides; then wash the member with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and treat each limb as it comes into its proper place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	 And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	 of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	 It happens rarely that the jaws are dislocated together, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: either they are a little removed from their place and softened a little; or they are completely dislocated and hang down towards the chest, and saliva flows from the mouth which he cannot hold, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue is entangled with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	 When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself through various dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is complete and accomplished, then you must quickly reset it, and do not delay; and in such a way that the assistant holds the patient's head, and the physician places his finger from one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and let the other two hands be ready to adjust; and instruct the patient to relax their jaw muscles and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	 And the physician must align it until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the setting is difficult, even if it is both jaws together, then soak them in hot water and oil until they are easily reset; do not delay the setting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are returned to their rightful place, and the patient's mouth is closed without softening, then place moistened cloths in a plaster made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bands; and let the patient sleep on his back, with his head between two cushions, so that he does not move to the right or left, nor should he try to talk, but let him eat light food until the pain is gone, and the jaws are tied; and then let him chew what he wants lightly, and do not work to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well tied and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	 And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place at one time, and are not returned to their proper places, then fever and customary swelling occur, and possibly abdominal discharge, and possibly vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	 And when you see this, then know that it is a serious condition; and many times he who experiences it dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	 of the forearm
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	 The forearm cannot dislocate from the inside or the outside of its continuity, and it is dislocated sometimes from weakness, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is such that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; then press the place strongly with your palm, and it will return; then apply the compress and bandage, and tighten it; and the shoulder cannot dislocate towards the outside; if not, and if it dislocates sometimes, reset it to its place, as we have said; then apply the compress and the bandage, and tighten it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is cured; and thus similarly is the shoulder brought back when it has left its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	 Of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 You should know that the shoulder is dislocated in only three ways: one way is that it dislocates at the bottom part of the shoulder; and the second way is at the top of the arm; and sometimes it dislocates at the top, but this happens rarely; and it does not dislocate to the back due to the shoulder, and it does not dislocate inward due to the nerves; and often it dislocates downwards towards the chest, especially for those who have little flesh, because for them it jumps quickly; for those who have enough flesh, it jumps with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	 And sometimes it happens to some people that they have a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated for this reason.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	 It is therefore necessary that you test it, until you are certain of it; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And the dislocation is known when it falls down towards the armpit, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a manifest diversity between them; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and under the armpit on the back of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move in any way; and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it manifestly on the back; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to reset when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	 And the method is that the minister lifts the hand of the patient up high, then places your fingers underneath, and raises the joint with force up to its place; and the minister lifts the hand, and extends it up, then places it underneath; so it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said within a few days, then the patient should be bathed in hot water; and the minister should use a softening and soothing ointment, such as a decoction of hollyhock and fenugreek and melilot in water, and apply it; then let the patient lie on their back, and place under the arm a pad of linen, not too soft nor too hard, then let the healer place his heel on the pad, and raise the head of the shoulder gently, and draw out the hand of the patient; and another minister should hold the head of the patient so that it does not move downwards; that shoulder will return immediately, and if you see this, reset it according to this method: and it is necessary for there to be present a man who is larger than the patient; and let him stand straight towards the side, and press his shoulder under the arm of the patient, and lift the arm up high, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister should draw the hand of the patient downwards towards the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too light, then put with him something heavy, and the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And it is rammed back in another way: and it is that one drives a long faggot into the ground, whose head is as round as a pistil, neither too thick nor too thin; then it is placed under the patient, but that he has soft cloths above, and the patient stands along the length of the stick; then his hand is stretched down on the other side in this manner, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not want to return for all these things that we have said, then perform this cure: take a faggot of two arm lengths and four fingers wide, which has the head round to enter deeply under the seat, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	 Then lie the patient on his back under a beam draped above, so that the beam does not hit the patient; then place it below the patient's buttocks; and stretch both arms along the beam, and bind the shoulder to the beam, and the arm at the wrist, then place the arm on the step of a wide ladder, and let the hand hang down, and let the body hang on the other side: the joint will now dislocate.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	 And when it is in place, however it may be, you must place under the buttocks an equal ball of wool; then apply the plaster prepared with flour from the mill, with incense and egg white, over all the shoulder and around; then hold it tightly under the buttocks, and turn the bandage on top of the plaster, and wrap the hand around its neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	 And it is necessary that he eats little food, so that the limb may be strengthened, for it will heal faster; and then eat more after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is stiffened and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the joint is moved out of place due to moisture that has come, or for another reason, it is necessary that you administer cautery through three holes, as it is stated in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	 And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after seven days, and the joint does not stay in place and cannot lift the arm upward, then know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place. ︎
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et endentement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	 And if after healing there is stiffness in the limb, and it comes on gradually with movement, then the patient should bathe many times until that stiffness is relieved, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	 of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	 Know that the shoulder joint is rarely dislocated, and rarely returns; and if it is dislocated in all directions, especially forward and backward, and the dislocation is not reduced, for one sees it well and feels it well; and it dislocates according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the sick shoulder with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 Because the joint is closed, and cannot bend the arm, nor reach the shoulder at all. ‌ ‌
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	 And it is necessary that you reset it before an abscess forms there, for if an abscess forms there, the setting will be difficult; and perhaps it cannot be set at all, especially when it is in the back; this is worse than other dislocations, and it causes greater pain, and death may occur.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	 And the restoration is thus: when it can be reset, you extend its hand with your two hands; and let its arms be spread, and place your hands around its elbow, above and below, and push the joint together, or at the root of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	 And if the dislocation is in front, it will return when he bends his hand to his hand, and strikes with the root of the palm the elbow that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; and it is that two assistants stretch the arm, and hold it by two assistants, so that it does not move during the extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a long and wide double cloth around it; and when the physician reaches the joint with his hand, he anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then strongly pushes the joint until it returns; and when it is in place, put on a dry poultice with some egg, and hold it firmly, and tie the arm around the patient's neck, and leave it for some days, then untie it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	 And if the joint is fixed in its place, release the ligament, and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not hold well, then start again with the bandage and the ligament, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is relieved; or you put on the joint a piece of fat mutton, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and make him enter the bath; and when he sweats, rub the joint gently, then put the fat back on, and then enter the bath; and do this two or three times, until it is healed; and if you see, put on moist heated cow dung mixed with butter, and hold it in place; thus it will return to its proper position.
li dislocation de la main	 The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	 The hand joint dislocates, and the return is light, more than other joints However, it must be returned to its place immediately in the same hour that it is dislocated, lest the place swell or hot abscess arise
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the reduction is such that you place the sick hand on a table, and the minister extends his hand, and the physician places it evenly, so that he puts his palm against the appearance of the joint, and presses until it returns However, you must check if it is well in place; then let the patient lay the back of their hand on the table for extension and reduction
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and the doctor place their hand over that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, that is good; if not, then hold it with soothing poultices on those abscesses, and leave it thus without repeating.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if he cannot bear it and you cannot put it in place after some days, the joint will remain crooked; nor does any harm come to the patient except that as long as the hand is dampened, it cannot grasp anything at all: then know that the nerves are cut or the arteries; there is no other device than to hold by cautery near the case, and perhaps there is no use in anything else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	 Et lorsque la main est en place, appliquez l'emplâtre dont nous avons parlé, puis serrez-le et laissez-le ainsi pendant 5 jours, puis desserrez-le et laissez-le ainsi.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he cannot move it well and there is some stiffness, then soak it in hot water and rub it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	 Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or on the inside; then stretch out the finger, and push the dislocation towards your thumb until it returns to its place, then support the head of the finger, and bend it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for 2 days, and then straighten it that day; and tie a bandage around it, as we have said, and remove the bandage the next day, and make it move, and rebandage it that night; and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the inside of the hand, and do as you did before, until it is healed; and do the same if it is dislocated on another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	 Dou dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	 When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, and there are several dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the sign is that the excrement jumps out without the will, nor can it be held, and often some member becomes flaccid, either the two thighs or the two arms or one, and often the spine moves in four parts; that which moves to the back is called "scoliosis": the cure is that you reverse if the scoliosis comes from childhood: then there will be no cure nor healing at all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancients describe cures in grand words, where there is not always great benefit; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the case of giddiness that comes to the chest beforehand, there is no reason or health; and likewise, that which comes straight to the two sides, and one cannot cure it except for that which properly comes to the back, as I say; and it should be that the patient is stretched on his back in a level place, and he has support underneath him so that he does not hurt himself; then drive a stake into the ground at the head, and another at the feet, and tie one cord under the patient's buttocks, and another at the hips, and at the knees, and at the ankles; and two assistants should know the cords, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two stakes; and they should be well tied, the stake as we have said, and the physician places his palms on the spine strongly, until it recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if it does not return with this cure, then take a table of three arms in length, and place it beneath the surface, and let the patient be on the side, and push the head of the table beneath the surface, then put the middle of the table upon the spine; and let the doctor place his feet upon the other end of the table, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do the same at the turnstile that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And it is that you drive two stakes into the head of the patient with an arm's length, and towards the feet, two others, and there should be between each stake, above and below, a palm's length; and in each stake there should be one hole, through which the pulley runs, and let the stakes be firmly in the ground so that they do not move; and between each two stakes there should be a turning stake, on which the rope turns, and between the two turnings there should be two small stakes of a palm's length to turn the pulley; and then tie the rope that is among the supports to the pulley towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other pulley, and each of the assistants turns his pulley all along the rope, and let the master place the spine equal as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is even, apply a desiccant plaster with plenty of egg, and then the compresses, and then the bandage of a tablet three fingers long, which should cover the place of jaundice and the healthy part of the spine, then tie with a ligature, as we have said, and let the patient have subtle nourishment until he is cured; and if anything happens at the end of the cure, administer softening and soothing medicines, with the bandage that we have mentioned before; sometimes one gives a piece of lead, and sometimes it appears in the back vertebrae of the spine, and one thinks it is dislocation; and it is the bone that bursts open, which is why one should not presume: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	 Of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	 Know that in the joints of the hip and the shoulder, dislocation occurs alone, not as in other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, front and back; it is dislocated more often within than without, and rarely in front or behind.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 And the sign of its inside dislocation is that when one joins the affected leg with the healthy one, it is longer and more open, and the patient's knee is more bent than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend his knee towards the fire; and the place which is near the swelling from the abscess is hot, because the head of the thigh bone comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	 And the sign of this one when it comes to lack, is that these events are contrary to the previous ones.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.
