And the sign of this one when it happens in front, is that he stretches his leg according to its length; however, do not bend the knee with pain, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot go forward, and he retains his urine, and his ankle swells, and when walking, he steps on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	 And the sign of this one when it happens behind is that he cannot extend his knee or bend it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the hip joint is in the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	 The return of this type of dislocation is that you consider if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its position, then there is no cure for it; and it is not necessary that there be any presumption about it.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	 And in that where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of four types of dislocation, then you hasten to turn the joint inside and out, and move it from right to left; perhaps it will return, and there is no need for any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	 And if it does not return in this manner, then it is necessary that you prepare one strong assistant, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or with one cord tied above the knee; and another assistant extends his hand on top in such a way that he places his hands under his armpits, then pulls a soft cord over the hip; and another holds the end of the cord; and they stretch up and down all at once, until the patient is lifted off the ground all at once, and remains hanging.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	 This manner of extension is common to four similarities, and if the dislocation returns, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	 If not, then it is necessary to apply a cure according to its similarity. When the dislocation is in the shoulder, it is necessary that you place the patient on his sound side, then place the ligature at the root of the thigh, and the place which is below the armpit, then extend the ligature upward towards the armpit and towards the ribs; then let another minister take his arms and embrace the large part of the unwell thigh, and stretch it very strongly: thus will it return to its place now; and this manner of dislocation is lighter than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	 And if you cannot close it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary that you tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong, soft ligature above the two heels, and above the two knees; and let the sick leg be extended two fingers more than the other; then let him hang from the top of a pole, and let it be two arms' length above the ground; then command one assistant to embrace the thigh at its head, and let another assistant hang with the patient, who strongly embraces the thigh, for the joint returns quickly now.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	 And when the dislocation is out, let the patient lie down as we have said for someone with gout, and tighten the ligature above the sick leg and also above the foot; then place two splints, one at the head and another at the feet; then insert a splint between the thighs of the patient in the middle; and let there be planted around moist rags, so that it does not wound the patient; then each assistant should extend towards him, and the doctor should bring the dislocation back into place with his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	 If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	 If not, place him on the table and press as we have said in the swelling, and let the patient lie on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	 And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to quickly extend the injured leg, as I have said; and let the physician place his hand on the injured ankle, then press with the other hand, and stretch down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And if the dislocation is in back, it is not necessary to extend the patient downwards or lift him off the ground, but he should be as if his hip were dislocated backwards, as we have said about lying on both hips; and let him lie on his face, and let the ligament be stretched as we have said before, and someone should press on the joint at the table; and it will be ready when the patient extends his legs, and they are equal; then bring the thighs together, and apply the plaster, and bind with a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let him rest for three days or four, then unbind, and apply the plaster again; and if you see that they are equal, then bind as before, and leave it for three days; then unbind, and let him walk well, until the limb is healed.
de la dislocation dou genoil	 Of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	 The knee is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, inside and out, and behind; it does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	 And the sign of this is that you instruct the patient to bend his leg at the thigh, and if it does not touch the thigh, know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee strongly; and another assistant extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that it touches the thigh lightly; and apply the bandage, and make the leg adhere to the thigh, and keep them together firmly for three days or four, then remove [the bandage]; and let the patient not move to go, as long as the limb is strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	 And if the limb is not at all, then administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	 of the dislocation of the ankle
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	 The ankles are sometimes swollen and completely dislocated, inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	 And the sign of this is that the ankle is swollen and protrudes forward in the part where it is dislocated; the reduction is easy, and one should extend it gently with their hands when it is only swollen.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	 And when it is completely dislocated, then you must make the patient sit upright, and have two assistants hold by the leg, above the ankle; then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then to the left twice, then extend it upwards, and firmly push the foot up; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, then repeat the work, for it will return; and if it cannot return thus, then make the patient lie on their back on the ground, and fix a firm stake in the ground between their thighs, and tie bands around it, so that it does not hurt the patient; then have one assistant hold the thigh, and another assistant extend the foot with their hands or a strap, which they tie above the ankle bone; then each assistant extends equally, and the stake should be immediately between the patient’s thighs to hold the patient when extending; then the physician places the dislocation evenly in his hands, and another assistant holds the sound leg below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	 And when it is ready, place the poultice and bandages on top, and bind firmly, and tie the foot to the leg, and protect the nerves that are above the ankle behind, so that the ligature is not too tight; then leave it for two days or three; and if the ligature softens, rebind; then untie on the third day or the fourth, and allow the patient to walk after four days; and if he goes before this time, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if abscesses come there, then you must treat them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
des dois	 of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	 When the toes are dislocated, you must straighten them gently without forcing, and this is a minor matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the dislocation is in any node of the foot's back, you must make the patient sit on a plain seat or on a straight table. Then put your foot on where these joints open, then press very hard with your foot until it returns; and when it is equal and nothing opens there, place under the sole of the foot a table with two legs, then hold it very tightly, and leave it for three days, then release it; and make him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	 of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	 When a wound comes with dislocation and one wants to restore it, it often happens that the patient dies: so do not be presumptuous in the cure if you are not wise in this art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not merciful and kind, and not bold; and at first use calming things on the abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then now reset the limb to its place before the abscess comes there; and when the limb is in place, administer calming things on the abscess, and treat the wound with desiccated ointments as is necessary; and if there is a fracture with the dislocation, and small bones are displaced, remove them, and do what we have said about simple diseases; and beware of entering into a path of fear, according to what I have said, for this avails you according to your Creator, and for the skill of your arms and body.
Amen	 Amen
